Not My Type

by Hexdealer

Summary

"She’s not my type," Agatha said firmly, crossing her arms.

Lilia raised an eyebrow, swirling her wine like a soap opera villain. "So you have a type? Do enlighten us."

Agatha groaned. "Fine. If you must know, I’m straight. And even if I wasn’t, Rio is at least ten years younger than me. I would never go there."

Cue Rio Vidal—Agatha’s insufferably smug, boundaryless neighbour—who has zero respect for personal space, steals her ice cream, wears her clothes, and now, apparently, needs a fake girlfriend for a work event.

Agatha should say no. She wants to say no. But somehow, she doesn’t.

Now she’s fake dating the most irritating woman alive, their friends are watching like it’s a spectator sport, and the walls between their apartments are very thin.

It’s fine. It’s fake. It’s strictly platonic.

…So why is Agatha’s stomach flipping every time Rio looks at her like that?

Or: Agatha insists she's straight, Rio insists on being a menace, and everyone else insists that there's a "vibe".

Chapter One

Agatha Harkness adjusted the strap of her handbag and plastered on her most professional smile as she unlocked the door to her apartment. Behind her, three colleagues followed, each so neatly put-together that her modest living room suddenly felt too small for all their tailored suits and gleaming shoes.

Before she could step inside, the sound of a spoon clinking against a bowl froze her in place. She knew that sound. It was the sound of betrayal.

Her eyes narrowed as she entered her apartment and rounded the corner to the kitchen. There, in all her smug glory, was Rio Vidal. She was bent over the counter, wearing Agatha’s plaid pyjama pants and an oversized sweatshirt—also Agatha’s. A bowl of chocolate fudge ice cream sat snugly in her left hand, half-devoured, the spoon dangling from her mouth as she rifled through a drawer.

Agatha had long considered herself a woman of composure, but this? This was testing her limits.

“What the hell are you doing?” Agatha hissed, keeping her voice low to avoid alerting her colleagues.

Rio’s brown eyes flicked up to meet Agatha’s, her lips curling around the spoon in her mouth into an infuriatingly casual smile as she mumbled, “Oh, hey! You’re back.” She tugged the spoon from her mouth and waved it lazily. “I’m looking for my vegetable peeler. You borrowed it weeks ago, remember?”

“Now?” Agatha’s voice pitched higher. She darted a glance toward the living room, where the muffled sounds of polite conversation continued. “You decided to break into my apartment now?”

“Technically, your spare key was under the mat. That’s practically an invitation,” Rio said, taking another leisurely bite of ice cream.

Agatha’s fingers curled into fists. “And the pyjamas?”

Rio looked down at herself, then shrugged. “Mine were in the wash, and these are comfy. You have good taste, by the way. Oh, also,” she gestured down to her bowl with the spoon, “you’re out of chocolate fudge.”

Agatha’s jaw almost dropped at the young girls audacity. She opened her mouth to fire back but was cut off by the sound of footsteps. One of her colleagues, Lilia, appeared in the doorway, her eyebrows shooting up at the sight of Rio.

“Oh, uh, I didn’t realise you had company, Agatha,” Lilia said, her gaze flicked between Agatha and Rio, curiosity written all over her face.

“I don’t,” Agatha said quickly, her cheeks burning. “Rio was just leaving.”

Rio, unbothered as ever, slid the drawer closed slowly with the ice cream still in hand. “Actually, I was just helping myself to a snack. Don’t mind me.”

“I do mind you,” Agatha snapped.

“Is she your... roommate?” Lilia asked, her tone far too amused for Agatha’s liking.

“No,” Agatha said firmly. “She’s my neighbour.”

“Best neighbour you’ll ever have,” Rio added with a wink, earning an amused look from Lilia.

Agatha’s glare could have set the ice cream on fire. She grabbed Rio by the arm and dragged her toward the door. “Out. Now.”

“Okay, okay. No need to be so uptight,” Rio said, though she didn’t seem remotely remorseful. As Agatha shoved her out into the hallway, Rio leaned back in with a grin, the bowl of ice cream still in her hand, “let me know when you find my peeler.”

The door slammed shut, cutting off Rio’s laughter. Agatha let out a sharp breath, tugged at her blazer, and turned back to her colleagues, trying to hold onto the last thread of composure.

“Sorry about that,” she said, voice tight but steady. “Shall we get started?”

Lilia smirked, eyes gleaming with mischief. “Your neighbour seems… fun.”

Agatha bit back a groan and slapped on another too-bright professional smile, teeth clenched.

***

Back in the living room, Lilia had already claimed the center of the couch, lounging with one leg tucked beneath her as if she owned the place. Jen was perched on the edge of the armchair, scrolling through her phone with the focus of someone plotting world domination, and Sharon had claimed a dining chair and dragged it closer to the coffee table, already sitting up straight with her notebook open like she was bracing for a board meeting.

Agatha sighed inwardly, knowing this was going to haunt her for weeks.

"Can I get anyone something to drink? Tea? Coffee?"

"Got wine?" Lilia asked, grinning like she already knew the answer.

Agatha gave her a flat look. "It’s two in the afternoon."

"And?" Lilia raised an eyebrow. "We’re not in a boardroom. Lighten up, Harkness. I’ll take red, if you’ve got it."

"I’ll pass," Jen mumbled, still staring at her phone. "But I’ll take tea. Something calming."
She glanced up, gave Agatha a once-over, then added, "If you’ve got anything in that category."

Agatha said nothing, choosing to ignore the thinly veiled jab, and turned to Sharon instead.

Sharon just smiled politely. "Tea would be lovely, thank you."

"Right," Agatha muttered, retreating to the kitchen. She grabbed mugs, filled the kettle, and—after a short internal war—yanked the wine bottle off the rack.

From the living room, Lilia’s voice carried through. "So, what’s the story with the neighbour?"

"Please don’t encourage this," Agatha called back, busying herself with the kettle.

"Oh, come on, Agatha," Lilia pressed. "She’s clearly into you."

"She’s not," Agatha said, re-entering the room with the tea tray and bottle of wine. She placed them on the table and began pouring, ignoring Lilia’s skeptical snort.

Lilia wasn’t about to let it go, not when she smelled blood in the water. She leaned back, swirling her wine like a soap opera villain.

"Oh, come on, Agatha. She was wearing your pyjamas, raiding your ice cream stash, and making herself at home in your kitchen. If that’s not a vibe, I don’t know what is."

Agatha set the teapot down with a little more force than necessary. "There is no vibe, Lilia. She’s just an obnoxious neighbour who doesn’t respect personal space."

"Obnoxious or not, she’s cute," Jen said without looking up from her phone.

Agatha crossed her arms tightly. "She’s not my type."

Lilia raised an eyebrow. "So, you have a type? Do enlighten us."

Sharon gave a soft chuckle into her teacup, saying nothing, but Agatha could tell she was quietly amused.

Agatha groaned. "Fine. If you must know, I’m straight. And even if I wasn’t, Rio is at least ten years younger than me. I would never go there."

The room fell silent for a beat, and Agatha thought, for a fleeting moment, she might have shut them up.

But then Lilia burst into laughter—a full, belly-deep laugh that made Jen finally glance up, smirking.

"Straight? Really, Agatha?" Lilia said, wiping a tear from her eye. "You? Oh, that’s rich."

"I am straight," Agatha insisted, her tone dangerously close to defensive. "And I have absolutely no interest in Rio. End of discussion."

"Oh, sure," Lilia drawled, raising her glass in a mock toast. "No interest at all in the hot younger neighbour who breaks into your apartment, steals your ice cream, and wears your pyjamas. You can say that, but I still think there's a vibe. Or maybe a fantasy."

"Maybe both," Jen muttered, her eyes returning to her phone.

Agatha scowled and threw her hands in the air. "Enough, both of you. Can we please focus on the proposal?"

Lilia rolled her eyes and took a swig of her wine, but Sharon gave her a sympathetic smile.

"Fine, fine," Lilia said, still chuckling as she set her glass down. "But don’t think this conversation is over."

"Oh, it absolutely is," Agatha muttered, pulling out her laptop and determinedly opening the presentation.

As the others settled into work mode, she tried to ignore the lingering smirks—and the tiny, traitorous part of her brain that wondered if Lilia might have a point. Absolutely not. 

Agatha clicked through the slides on her laptop, her voice steady as she walked her colleagues through the finer points of the proposal. On the surface, she appeared calm, collected, and entirely in control. But beneath the surface, her thoughts churned like a stormy sea.

Straight, she reaffirmed internally, repeating it like a mantra as she adjusted the presentation screen.

Just because Lilia had a flair for making everything sound like a romantic comedy plotline didn’t mean there was any truth to it. Agatha had dated men. Married one, for god's sake. Sure, she hadn't really dated since the divorce, but that didn't mean anything.

She was just busy.

She was focused.

She was straight.

She was...

Her mind flitted briefly to her upcoming date tomorrow night—the one she had almost forgotten she had agreed to. A handsome man—smart, charming, her age. It was promising. She even liked the way he held doors open without making it feel patronising. That had to count for something.

But then, hadn’t the last couple of rare dates also seemed promising? Each one had started with the same cocktail of hope and cautious optimism, only to fizzle out when things inevitably fell flat. Too clingy. Too detached. Too obsessed with cryptocurrency. Why do they all talk about cryptocurrency?

Agatha clicked to the next slide, forcing herself to focus on Lilia’s questions about the budget.

"We can repurpose some of the existing resources," she said evenly, highlighting the section in question. "It’s all outlined here."

Lilia nodded along, but her smirk hadn’t entirely faded.

Agatha pretended not to notice and continued.

It’s not that I’m picky, she thought defensively. I just have standards. Reasonable ones. And tomorrow’s date will go better. He’s nice. Normal. Predictable. A grown-up.

Her fingers hovered over the trackpad as another, unwelcome thought bubbled to the surface.

Unlike Rio.

Agatha clenched her jaw, willing her mind to let it go. She wasn’t going to entertain that absurdity, not after Lilia’s teasing.

So what if Rio had a certain… charm?

A reckless, infuriating charm that made her want to throttle her one second and maybe... No.

Absolutely not.

Rio was young, careless, and entirely too pleased with herself. She wasn’t even in the running.

"Agatha, are you listening?"

Jen’s voice cut through her inner spiral. Agatha blinked, realising Lilia was watching her with a knowing expression.

"Of course," she replied briskly, gesturing to the chart on the screen. "As I was saying, the projections show…"

Her voice carried on, but her thoughts had already rebelled.

She told herself it was because Lilia’s ribbing had gotten under her skin, not because Rio’s grin and her smug, comfortable presence in Agatha’s kitchen had left an impression.

Not because Rio made her laugh—no, smirk. Briefly. Begrudgingly.

Straight. Straight as an arrow.

And tomorrow’s date was going to be perfect.

At least, she hoped so.

***

The restaurant buzzed with soft conversation and the clinking of silverware. Agatha sat across from Ralph Bohner, a man who, by all accounts, was perfect on paper. Tall, well-dressed, with a friendly smile that hovered somewhere between charming and wholesome. He spoke with ease, regaling her with stories about his work as a structural engineer and his recent hiking trip to the Adirondacks.

Agatha listened attentively, nodding and offering the occasional laugh at the right moments. Ralph was everything she had told herself she wanted. A grown-up. Normal. Predictable. Not a single ounce of chaos.

And yet.

She swirled the last of her wine in the glass, trying to pinpoint the emptiness that sat stubbornly in her chest. Ralph was handsome. Smart. Sweet, even. But every time he smiled at her, she felt... nothing. No spark. No warmth. Just the faint itch of polite obligation.

"And that's when I realised I’d been reading the map upside down the whole time," Ralph finished with a chuckle, his brown eyes crinkling at the corners.

Agatha forced a laugh, setting down her glass. "That sounds like quite the adventure."

"It was," he said, leaning forward slightly. "But enough about me. What about you? Any big plans for the weekend?"

"Oh, nothing exciting," she said, fiddling with the napkin in her lap. "Just work, mostly."

Ralph nodded, his gaze lingering on her face. "You’re really something, Agatha. Smart, successful, gorgeous. I feel like I hit the jackpot just being here tonight."

The compliment landed as it should—flattering, sincere—but all Agatha could muster was a tight smile. "That’s kind of you to say."

The evening wrapped up soon after, with Ralph insisting on walking her back to her apartment.

The chill of the evening air nipped at Agatha’s cheeks as they strolled down the quiet street. Ralph’s easy conversation filled the silence, but her thoughts were elsewhere. She knew she should feel something—anything—for him. He was everything she claimed to want. So why did it feel like she was trying to jam a puzzle piece into the wrong space?

"This is me," she said, stopping in front of her building and fishing for her keys. "Thank you for tonight, Ralph. It was... nice."

"Nice?" Ralph teased with a grin. "I’ll take it."

Before she could offer an apologetic smile, the sound of footsteps made her stiffen. She didn’t need to turn around to know who it was.

"Well, well," Rio’s voice drawled, dripping with mischief. "Who’s this?"

Agatha clenched her teeth, silently willing the ground to swallow her whole. She turned to find Rio standing in her plaid pyjamas again, hands shoved casually into the pockets of her jacket. Only Rio would be standing outside their apartment building in pyjamas. Rio’s gaze flicked between Agatha and Ralph, a smirk curling her lips.

"Uh, Ralph," he said, holding out a hand. "Ralph Bohner."

Rio’s eyebrows shot up, and Agatha could see the joke forming before it even left her mouth. See? Immature.

"Bohner?" Rio repeated, her smirk widening. "As in—?"

"Yes, that’s my last name," Ralph cut in good-naturedly. "Heard it all before."

"I bet you have," Rio said with a chuckle as she shook his offered hand. "I’m Rio, by the way. Agatha’s best neighbour ever."

"Ah," Ralph said, clearly unsure how to respond to Rio’s energy. He turned back to Agatha, his expression softening. "Well, I had a great time tonight. Maybe we can do this again?"

Agatha forced a smile, her stomach twisting. "Maybe."

Ralph leaned in, brushing a polite kiss to her cheek before waving to Rio and heading down the street.

As soon as he disappeared around the corner, Agatha let out a long breath. Her chest felt heavy, her mind racing. She should have felt something, she told herself. Ralph was perfect. Kind, thoughtful, handsome. But her heart had stubbornly refused to cooperate.

"Bohner," Rio said, breaking into her thoughts. She snorted, leaning against the side of the building. "You sure know how to pick em."

"Goodnight, Rio," Agatha said, her tone clipped as she pushed through the entrance doors.

Agatha barely made it two steps into the lobby when Rio darted in behind her, letting the door swing shut with an obnoxious clang. Agatha stopped, her shoulders tensing as she turned to face the relentless woman.

"Why are you following me?" she asked, her voice strained.

"Following you? Please," Rio said, flashing her a grin. "I live here too, remember? Just happened to be out for some fresh air when you returned from your very... eventful date."

"Eventful?" Agatha echoed, exasperated. "He walked me home. That’s it."

"Sure, but his name was Bohner," Rio said, drawing out the syllables as though savouring them. "I mean, come on, Aggie. That’s comedy gold."

Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose. "It’s not Aggie, and I don’t have the energy for this tonight."

Rio’s grin only widened as she trailed behind Agatha toward the stairs. Agatha had hoped that the stairs would deter her from following, but of course they didn't. "What’s wrong? Bohner not the one? Or did I scare him off?"

"He’s perfectly fine," Agatha said, her steps brisk as she climbed the stairs. "Handsome, smart, polite. Everything a woman could want."

"Except for you, apparently," Rio said, easily keeping pace. "Don’t tell me you’re one of those people who self-sabotage when things get too boring."

Agatha stopped abruptly on the landing, spinning to glare at Rio. "What is your point?"

Rio raised her hands in mock surrender, her expression frustratingly amused. "No point. Just making conversation. You looked like you could use a distraction."

"A distraction?" Agatha echoed, her voice sharp. "You’re always a distraction."

Rio smirked, pressing her tongue into the inside of her cheek, eyes glinting.
"You’re welcome."

Agatha groaned, turning back toward her apartment door. She fumbled for her keys, already dreaming of the peace and quiet that awaited her inside. The key had barely turned in the lock when she felt Rio step closer, the warmth of her presence brushing against her back.

"And for the record," Rio said, her voice dropping to a teasing lilt, "if you’re into older guys with unfortunate last names, you could at least warn me before I meet them. I need prep time."

Agatha shoved the door open and stepped inside, her jaw clenched. "Goodnight, Rio."

Before she could close the door, Rio caught it with her foot and slipped inside like she owned the place.

"Oh no, you’re not getting rid of me that easily," Rio said, sauntering toward the kitchen and rummaging through a cabinet as if she lived there. "You owe me an explanation for why you keep dating guys who put you to sleep."

Agatha gaped at her. "I don’t owe you anything, least of all a play-by-play of my love life."

“Love life?” Rio snorted, pulling out a box of crackers and waving it at her. “Please. That wasn’t love, Aggs, that was two people pretending dinner counts as intimacy."

"Out," Agatha snapped, pointing toward the door.

Rio smirked, leaning casually against the counter as she popped a cracker into her mouth. "You’re so uptight. You should thank me for making your night more interesting."

Agatha grabbed the box from her hands, her patience finally snapping. "Rio. Get. Out."

"Fine," Rio said, holding up her hands in surrender again. "But just so you know, you could do better. Bohner’s not your type."

"And what, you think you know my type?" Agatha demanded, her patience thin.

Rio didn’t answer right away. Instead, she tilted her head, her smirk softening into something almost serious. "Maybe. Maybe not. But I know it’s not him."

The intensity in Rio’s gaze made Agatha’s stomach flip, and she hated how disarmed she felt. Before she could formulate a response, Rio turned and strolled toward the door, her usual swagger firmly back in place.

"Sleep tight, Aggie," Rio called over her shoulder as she slipped out.

Agatha locked the door behind her with more force than necessary, leaning against it with a frustrated sigh. She knew Rio was right. Bohner was not her type. No matter how badly she wanted him to be.

Chapter Two

Agatha sat at her desk at the consulting firm, staring at the stack of reports she hadn’t touched since lunch. Her inbox was full. Her calendar was worse. Another day of chasing clients who didn’t reply, rewriting briefs that didn’t need rewriting, and sitting through meetings that could’ve been emails.

Her phone buzzed—an email from Lilia.

Subject: Next time, more enthusiasm.

Agatha didn’t even open it. She just let out a short laugh and leaned back in her chair. It was the third jab this week. Maybe fourth. Jen had left a dozen comments on yesterday’s report, all vague and passive.

Sharon had forwarded some client feedback that morning with a note that read “worth keeping in mind going forward,” which somehow made Agatha want to launch her monitor out the window.

Everything felt pointless. No matter how hard she worked, it wasn’t enough. And she was tired in a way that sleep didn’t fix.

Ralph had been the high point of her week. Which said... a lot. A dinner that left her cold, a goodnight kiss she didn’t feel, and a polite text she never responded to.

Maybe it wasn’t the job. Maybe it wasn’t them.

“Maybe it’s me,” she muttered, snapping her laptop shut like it might stop her from thinking.

A soft knock came before Lilia pushed her office door open and leaned against the frame, her usual smirk in place.

“God, you look like shit,” she said cheerfully. “Rough day?”

“You could say that.”

“Well, perfect. We’re going out.”

Agatha blinked. “Out?”

“Drinks. Dancing. It's Friday and you clearly need a reset.”

Agatha shook her head and turned back to tidying the papers on her desk, mostly to avoid making eye contact. “I don’t dance.”

Jen appeared next, adjusting the sleeves of her pastel blazer like she was about to step into a TED talk. “You don’t have to dance. You just have to come. Sharon’s already in.”

“I have work—”

Sharon stepped in last, as if summoned by name, holding a cup of herbal tea and wearing that unsettlingly serene smile. “You’re coming,” she said gently. “We’ve decided.”

Agatha stared at them. She didn’t have the energy to argue.

“Seven o’clock,” Lilia said, already halfway back into the hallway. “And wear something that doesn’t scream I do my taxes for fun.”

Agatha didn’t respond. Just sat there, watching the door slowly swing shut behind them.

And that’s how she ended up here, tugging at the hem of her plum coloured blouse, feeling out of place as she followed her colleagues into a trendy downtown bar. The space was loud, packed with people, and pulsing with music. Lilia had already disappeared toward the bar to order drinks, while Sharon and Jen scoped out a table near the back.

“This is not my scene,” Agatha muttered, trailing behind them. She didn’t think it was any of their scene.

Jen turned to her with a smirk. “Oh, come on, Agatha, you need to loosen up. Get your mind off work for once.”

“Right,” Agatha said dryly, glancing around at the crowd. She was pretty sure this place had more hipster vibes than she could handle, but the last thing she wanted was to feel like the office oddball.

As they found their seats, Agatha sat down with a sigh, scanning the room, trying to ignore the familiar feeling of discomfort settling in. She was already trying to decide how much longer she would have to stay when Lilia reappeared with a round of drinks.

“There you go, darling,” Lilia said, sliding a gin and tonic toward Agatha. “This should help.”

“Thanks,” Agatha said with a weak smile. She picked it up, grateful for the distraction. After a sip, she forced a laugh at something Sharon was saying, but it wasn’t long before her drink was empty and she needed a break from the group. She excused herself and made her way toward the bar.

The bar was even louder up close, with groups of people spilling out into the space around it. Agatha stood at the counter, trying to catch the bartender’s eye. She shifted uncomfortably from one foot to the other, feeling self-conscious in her blouse and pencil skirt, wondering if she was overdressed or underdressed for this kind of night. Maybe she should have taken Lilia’s advice and gone more casual.

A voice cut through the noise. “Hey, beautiful. What’s your name?”

Agatha’s stomach dropped as she turned to find a guy leaning against the bar next to her. He had that kind of smirk on his face that immediately made her uncomfortable, like he thought he knew everything about her with one glance. His eyes traced her up and down with too much familiarity and she bristled.

She took a step back, clutching the edge of the bar tighter. “Uh… not interested,” she muttered, trying to sidestep him.

“Oh, come on, don’t be like that, sweetheart. I can buy you a drink—”

She was about to shoot him down again when, out of nowhere, she felt a presence beside her. A hand casually slid around her waist, pulling her closer and her body tensed, instinctively bracing for whatever was coming next. She opened her mouth to protest, but before she could say anything, the person leaned in, speaking in a low voice.

“She said she wasn’t interested,” came the smooth, firm voice.

Agatha froze, her head snapping to the woman attached to her, her heart beating faster as she realised who it was.

Rio.

Rio’s arm was around her waist, the contact so natural, like it was something she had every right to do. The guy at the bar blinked, clearly taken aback by the sudden intervention, but he didn’t back down.

“Probably don’t even know each other,” he muttered, his gaze shifting between them with a doubtful smirk. “Girls do this all the time. Pretend to be with someone just to get rid of guys.”

Agatha could feel her heart racing, a mix of surprise and something else she couldn’t quite place. She was about to open her mouth to tell this guy off, but before she could, Rio’s grip tightened slightly, pulling her even closer and Agatha hated the way her breath stuttered.

“You’re wrong,” Rio said, her voice laced with calm but undeniable authority. “She’s not interested, and I am her girlfriend. So why don’t you take your drink and find someone else to bother?”

Agatha stared at her, her eyes wide. She had never seen Rio like this before—so confident, so assertive. It was as if she had flipped a switch, becoming someone entirely different from the playful, easy-going, annoying neighbour she thought she knew. There was no hesitation in her words, no room for argument. Rio was firmly in control of the situation and Agatha felt her face heat up.

The guy looked between the two of them, his expression faltering, before he muttered something under his breath. He looked at Agatha one last time, clearly not willing to challenge Rio any further, and walked away.

Agatha was left standing there, completely speechless. She hadn’t expected Rio to step in like that, to act as if she owned the situation, and her chest tightened at the thought. Rio, her neighbour, who was so carefree and annoyingly charming one minute, had just acted like someone who would defend her, possessively almost.

“You…” Agatha started, unsure how to finish the sentence. “You really just did that.”

Rio shifted back just enough to let her arm slide off Agatha’s waist, but she didn’t go far. She tilted her head slightly, tongue pressing into the inside of her cheek as she gave Agatha a once-over—like she was sizing her up and enjoying the view.

“Yeah,” she said, voice low and dry. “Guess I’ve got a soft spot for women who look like they’re two seconds from throat-punching someone.”

Agatha blinked. The guy was gone, but she could still feel the tension he left behind—only now it had morphed into something else entirely. Heavier. Closer. The air between her and Rio felt charged in a way that made it hard to think clearly.

And somehow, she wasn’t uncomfortable.

She felt... relieved.

Maybe it was because Rio had stepped in. Or maybe it was the way she’d done it—casual, quiet, a hand at her waist like it belonged there. Like Agatha wasn’t just being helped, but claimed.

“Thanks,” she muttered finally, unsure why the word felt so small.

Rio raised an eyebrow. “You’re welcome.” Her voice dipped lower as she leaned in again, just enough. “But you owe me.”

That pulled Agatha right out of whatever daze she’d been stuck in.

She straightened, cleared her throat. “Owe you?” she repeated, rolling her eyes. “What, for stepping in uninvited? Don’t act like I asked.”

Rio didn’t flinch. She just smirked, shifting her weight lazily like she had all night. “You looked at him like you weren’t sure whether to run or set him on fire. I chose the option with fewer witnesses.”

Agatha snorted before she could stop herself, then immediately tried to bury it. “I can handle myself.”

“I know,” Rio said.

Of course she did. She always did. Always just that little bit ahead—smug, infuriating, probably enjoying this.

Agatha crossed her arms. She could tell Rio wasn’t taking her seriously, and honestly? Fine. She wasn’t sure she even meant what she’d said. That whole moment—whatever it was—had thrown her off.

Her stomach still hadn’t settled. That fluttery feeling was still hanging around, completely uninvited.

She glanced over.

Rio was at the bar now, one hand resting on the edge, chatting with the bartender like she’d been here a hundred times. The jacket she was wearing was new—black, fitted, unfair. Her jeans looked expensive in that subtle, lived-in way. And the boots were... a choice.

It wasn’t the Rio she was used to. No messy hair. No old sweatshirt. None of that casual, half-distracted energy.

This was... put-together. Intentional. Sharp.

And hot.

Agatha stared a second too long.

Then she caught herself and looked away fast, shaking her head like that would clear it.

No. Nope.

Rio was not hot.

“What are you even doing here?” she asked, her voice a little sharper than she meant. “I didn’t know you frequented to bars.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, matching Agatha's tone with a slight smirk. “I could ask you the same thing,” she shot back, her voice dripping with amusement.

Agatha blinked, surprised. “What, you think I don’t belong here?” she shot back, a little defensive, but Rio’s playful challenge only made her feel more out of place.

“I didn’t say that” Rio teased, her smirk widening as she leaned casually against the bar. “I just didn’t take you for the bar type. But I guess you can surprise me every now and then.”

She leaned in a little closer to Agatha, her eyes twinkling with something that she couldn’t quite figure out. Agatha narrowed her eyes, her pulse quickening at the way Rio leaned into her space like it was the most natural thing in the world.

“Well, I’m not here for the ambiance—I’m here because my coworkers practically dragged me.”

Rio tilted her head, her smirk never faltering. “That explains why you’re clinging to the bar like it’s a life raft.” She gestured toward the rest of the group, now laughing and chatting at a table across the room. “You don’t seem like the mingling type.”

Agatha bristled, her pride prickling. “I can mingle just fine, thank you.”

“Uh-huh,” Rio said, unconvinced. She took a sip from her drink, her eyes sparkling with that maddening mix of challenge and amusement. “I’ll believe it when I see it.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but her retort caught in her throat as Rio shifted her stance, drawing Agatha’s attention again. She had to admit—reluctantly—that Rio looked... good tonight. Not hot. Just… good.

It was unfair, really, how effortlessly Rio could command a room, even one as loud and chaotic as this bar. Agatha’s gaze flicked to Rio’s face, catching the raised eyebrow Rio shot back at her, clearly catching her staring.

Agatha scowled. “What?”

“Nothing,” Rio said, though her grin suggested otherwise. She set her drink down on the bar, shifting her full attention to Agatha. “So, if you’re not here for the ambiance and clearly not for the mingling, why did you let them drag you here?”

Agatha huffed, crossing her arms. “To avoid feeling like a social outcast when Lilia and Jen gossip about how boring I am on Monday.”

Rio let out a low chuckle. “Ah, workplace peer pressure. Say no more.” She leaned her elbow on the bar, her expression softening slightly. Rio swirled her drink absently, her gaze flickering to the bustling crowd before landing back on Agatha. “Speaking of workplace dynamics,” she started slowly, her tone suddenly casual but with a faint undertone of annoyance, “I’ve got this work Christmas party in two weeks.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “And? Don’t tell me you’re one of those people who actually likes holiday parties.”

Rio smirked. “Not even close. But this one’s mandatory, and…” She hesitated, a rare flicker of discomfort crossing her face. “There’s this colleague of mine. Let’s just say they’re a bit too touchy for my liking.”

Agatha blinked, surprised by the admission. It wasn’t often that Rio let her guard down, even slightly. “Touchy how?” she asked, her voice softening despite herself, her focus zeroing in on Rio.

“You know,” Rio said, waving a hand vaguely, “the kind of person who doesn’t seem to understand personal space. Always leaning in too close, brushing against you when it’s completely unnecessary, that sort of thing.”

Agatha frowned, her annoyance at Rio momentarily forgotten. “That sounds... awful. Have you said anything to them?”

“I’ve tried,” Rio said, her tone turning wry. “But they just laugh it off, like I’m joking or being overly sensitive. It’s honestly exhausting.”

Agatha studied Rio’s face, noting the way her usual confidence seemed tempered by frustration. It was strange to see her like this—vulnerable, in a way that felt almost... human. Huh, who knew she had that capability.

“So what are you going to do?” Agatha asked, genuinely curious, stepping closer to hear her more clearly over the bar’s noise.

Rio glanced at her, a mischievous glint returning to her eyes. “Well, I was thinking of bringing someone along. You know, as a ‘hands-off’ warning sign.”

Agatha snorted. “Like a human shield?”

“Exactly,” Rio said, grinning now. “Someone who can handle themselves, keep things light, and make it crystal clear that I’m not available for unsolicited contact.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “And have you found your lucky human shield yet?”

Rio leaned closer, her fingers reaching out to gently play Agatha’s blouse just above her hip, her grin widening. “Not yet. But I might have a candidate in mind.”

Agatha froze, realising where this was going. “Oh, no,” she said quickly, holding up her hands and taking a small step back, Rio’s hand dropping back to her side. “Don’t even think about it.”

“Why not?” Rio said, feigning innocence. “You’d be perfect. You’re sharp, quick-witted, and hot. Triple threat. I’d need to make it believable.”

Agatha's mouth opened, then closed, completely caught off guard by the unexpected compliment buried in Rio’s teasing tone. Her face heated up despite herself, and she quickly crossed her arms to regain some semblance of control.

“I’m not your ‘perfect’ anything,” she retorted, narrowing her eyes. “Find someone else to play pretend with.”

Rio tilted her head, her smirk deepening. “Oh, come on. After tonight? You kind of owe me.”

Agatha groaned and she threw her head back dramatically.

Rio’s grin turned positively smug. “If it weren’t for me, who knows how long he would’ve kept pestering you…”

Agatha scowled. “I had it handled.”

“Sure you did,” Rio said, her tone dripping with mock agreement. “Because looking like a deer caught in headlights is totally an effective defence strategy.”

“I was not—” Agatha started to snap, but then stopped herself, biting back the retort. She exhaled slowly through her nose, glaring at Rio. “You’re very irritating.”

“I’m just offering you a chance to repay the favour,” Rio said, her expression the picture of innocence, though the mischievous sparkle in her eyes betrayed her true intentions.

Agatha huffed, turning away from Rio as if she could physically escape the conversation. “This is ridiculous,” she muttered, more to herself than to Rio.

“Think of it this way,” Rio continued, leaning her elbow against the bar as she watched Agatha with infuriating amusement. “You’d be helping me out, and you’d get to make some awkward work party at least mildly entertaining.”

Agatha shot her a sidelong glance. “Entertaining how? I’m finding it hard to find anything that is beneficial for me in this ‘arrangement’.”

Rio shrugged, her grin softening into something more genuine. “Well, I’m sure we could come up with a few ways to keep it interesting and to make sure there’s something in it for you.”

Agatha’s stomach flipped, but she set her jaw, forcing her expression into something unimpressed. If Rio noticed anything, she didn’t show it. She rolled her eyes instead, shaking her head. “You are unbelievable. My condition is that you stop breaking into my apartment.”

“Unbelievably charming, maybe,” Rio quipped, earning herself a sharp look from Agatha as she avoided Agatha’s condition.

“You’re lucky I don’t smack that smirk right off your face,” Agatha muttered, though there was no real heat behind her words.

Rio straightened, holding her hands up in mock surrender. “Alright, alright. No pressure. Just... think about it.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes at her. She should have said no. Instead, she said nothing at all.

Agatha shook her head and took a deliberate step back, trying to create some distance—both physical and mental—from Rio’s overwhelming presence. She could feel her colleagues’ gazes burning into her from across the bar and realised how long she’d been gone. If she didn’t return soon, they would undoubtedly spin this into a Monday morning story she didn’t need.

“I should get back to my group before they think I ditched them,” she said, her tone brisk.

“Good idea,” Rio said with a teasing lilt, as though she made it clear she didn’t believe Agatha wanted to leave at all.

Agatha turned to go, but Rio’s voice stopped her in her tracks. “See you at home later, Aggie.”

Agatha froze for a fraction of a second before glancing back over her shoulder. Rio stood there, grinning in that infuriating way she always did, like she had the upper hand in a game Agatha wasn’t even sure she was playing.

Agatha just rolled her eyes and turned back towards her colleagues.

Agatha navigated her way through the crowd, the noise and bustle of the bar doing little to drown out the lingering warmth of Rio’s words. God, that woman was annoying.

When Agatha reached her table, she was immediately met with Lilia’s smirk. The woman didn’t say anything at first, just sipped her drink, her eyes sparkling with amusement.

Jen, however, wasn’t as subtle. She leaned forward with a grin. “Wasn’t that your nosy neighbour? The one we met last week? You know, the one who looked entirely too comfortable in your apartment?”

Agatha set her empty glass she was fiddling with, all that time at the bar and she didn’t get another drink, down with more force than necessary, ignoring the sudden heat creeping up her neck. “She wasn’t comfortable,” Agatha said quickly, too quickly. “She was just… there.”

Lilia raised an eyebrow, her smirk widening. “Oh, she was definitely comfortable.”

Agatha glared at them, feeling her patience thin. “Can we not do this right now? She’s just… Rio. She’s always around because she doesn’t have boundaries, not because there’s anything going on.”

Jen snorted into her drink. “Sure, nothing’s going on. That’s why she was standing so close to you just now. I’m sure that was completely platonic.”

Lilia leaned her chin on her hand, looking entirely too entertained. “She did seem pretty invested. If I didn’t know better, I’d think she was staking a claim or something.”

Agatha groaned, burying her face in her hands. “I hate all of you.”

“Love you too,” Jen said brightly, clinking her glass with Lilia’s.

The conversation mercifully shifted after that, but Agatha couldn’t shake the feeling of being watched—or the knowing looks Lilia occasionally threw her way. She distracted herself by eating the ice from her glass and nodding along to whatever Sharon was saying.

***

Agatha found herself fumbling with her keys at her apartment door a little after midnight. The buzz from the drinks she’d had with her colleagues made her clumsier than usual. She muttered a curse under her breath as she missed the lock for the third time, leaning heavily against the doorframe for balance.

The distant ding of the elevator caught her attention. She glanced over, squinting in the dim hallway lighting, and her stomach dropped, and she had to sudden urge to vomit.

Rio stumbled out of the elevator, her arm draped around a woman Agatha didn’t recognise. The woman was tall and effortlessly elegant, her laughter soft and melodic as she leaned into Rio’s side.

Agatha froze, watching as Rio adjusted her hold on the woman, steadying both of them. They were clearly tipsy—the kind of drunk where everything seemed funny, and the world tilted a little too much.

“Careful there,” Rio said with a low chuckle, her voice carrying down the hall. She was grinning, her usual confidence somehow even more pronounced in her loosened state.

Agatha’s chest tightened. She quickly turned back to her door, fumbling more aggressively with her keys. She didn’t want to be caught standing there, gawking like an idiot.

But, of course, Rio noticed her.

“Well, well,” Rio drawled, her tone dripping with amusement. “If it isn’t my favourite neighbour.”

Agatha felt a mix of frustration and embarrassment as she forced the door open, trying her best to ignore Rio’s presence. But Rio wasn’t going to make it easy.

Agatha sighed and muttered under her breath, “Could you keep it down? Some of us have to actually get up in the morning.” She winced at how sharp her tone came out. The alcohol wasn’t helping her control her words.

Rio raised an eyebrow, her smirk practically audible. “Oof, somebody’s grumpy.” She leaned a little closer to her companion, her voice dropping lower but still loud enough for Agatha to hear. “Maybe she needs to get laid or something. All that uptight energy’s gotta go somewhere.”

Agatha’s eyes widened, the words cutting deeper than she expected. She snapped her head toward Rio, her face flushed with annoyance and alcohol-induced warmth. “Excuse me?”

Rio shrugged, unfazed by Agatha’s sudden defensiveness. “What? I’m just saying. You’re always so… tense. A little fun wouldn’t kill you. Might actually be beneficial.” She shot a playful glance at the woman at her side, who laughed softly.

Agatha’s mind raced, the mix of irritation and self-consciousness hitting her all at once. She glared at Rio, struggling to find the right words. “I’m not uptight or tense. I’m just not an idiot who brings random people back at all hours of the night.”

“Oh, please,” Rio retorted, her voice dripping with amusement. “You can pretend you don’t care, but I think you’re just mad you’re not the one getting all my attention.”

Agatha's heart skipped a beat, her anger boiling over, but she kept her cool as best as she could. “Just…keep it down. I don’t need a play-by-play of your... whatever this is,” she shot back, finally stepping fully into her apartment and closing the door behind her with a little more force than necessary.

The sound of her heart pounding in her chest was almost drowned out by the ringing in her ears. What she would do to wrap her hands around that woman’s throat.

She kicked off her shoes with a huff, the alcohol beginning to make her head spin a little. It had been a long night—her colleagues’ incessant chatter, Lilia’s teasing, Jen’s comments—and now Rio’s ridiculous antics. She didn’t know why it irritated her so much. She barely knew the woman. Sure, she was annoying as hell, but she wasn’t even worth this level of frustration. Why couldn’t Agatha just let it go?

After a few moments of stumbling around, she managed to get herself ready for bed. She tugged at the hem of her blouse, yanking it over her head with a slight wince, still a little off-balance from the drinks. She had meant to keep it short and get some rest, but as she climbed into bed, something in her mind kept replaying the conversation with Rio. She groaned in annoyance and rolled over, trying to shake it off.

The silence of her apartment should have been calming, but just as she was starting to drift off, there it was—the unmistakable sound of muffled laughter. It wasn’t loud enough to be intrusive, but it was there. And then… a moan. Soft but distinct.

Agatha’s eyes snapped open, the warmth of alcohol evaporating into a cold, prickling feeling as she froze in her bed. The wall. It was only a wall separating her bedroom from Rio’s.

And Rio knew that. She knew the layout of their apartments.

The realisation settled uncomfortably in Agatha’s stomach. She closed her eyes tightly, trying to block out the sounds, but it was impossible. Every time she thought it would stop, it didn’t. She was painfully aware of the proximity, the thin wall between them doing nothing to soften the sounds of Rio’s evening activities.

This is ridiculous, Agatha thought, her face flushed with a mix of anger and frustration. She threw her pillow over her head, hoping to drown it all out, but it didn’t work. The muffled noises seemed to invade her space anyway, making her even more irritable.

She had told Rio to keep it down. She had made it clear she didn’t want to hear any of this. Yet here she was, trapped in her own apartment, trying to ignore the sounds of her annoying neighbour having what sounded like a great time.

Agatha let out a frustrated sigh and pulled the pillow off her head, staring at the ceiling, her mind racing with all the reasons she shouldn’t care. She didn’t care.

Chapter Three

The morning light sliced through the blinds in thin, golden slats, landing directly across Agatha’s face. She groaned, rolling onto her side in a futile attempt to escape it. Her head throbbed—a slow, punishing rhythm—and her stomach churned with the sour remnants of cheap tequila.

Brilliant decision-making, as always.

She cracked one eye open, immediately regretting it. Last night had been a blur of laughter, clinking glasses, and Jen’s relentless insistence on "just one more round." Agatha hadn’t planned on drinking that much, but somewhere between the peer pressure and the electric energy of the bar, she’d stopped keeping track.

Dragging herself upright, she winced at the stiffness in her limbs. The apartment was mercifully quiet—no unexpected guests, no reminders of last night’s questionable choices. She shuffled toward the bathroom, the cool tiles sending a shiver up her spine. The mirror wasn’t kind. Her eyes were shadowed, her skin paler than usual, and her hair was a tangled testament to a restless night.

As she splashed water on her face, flashes of the evening flickered in her mind. The music, the heat, the pulse of conversation. And Rio.

That smirk, the way she leaned in just a little too close, the challenge in her voice. There had been something different last night—something that felt like an unspoken dare. Or maybe it was just the alcohol playing tricks on her.

Get it together, Agatha.

She brushed off the thought as she tugged on a faded band tee and loose jeans, padding into the kitchen where the coffee machine whirred to life. The rich scent filled the space, a small comfort against the dull headache still gnawing at her skull. She took a slow sip, staring out the window, trying to shake the lingering haze.

She needed a distraction. And the bookstore—her sanctuary—was calling.

-

By the time she got home at 2 p.m., the morning’s peace had been replaced by the buzz of the city, the distant hum of traffic, and the warmth of a full stomach from lunch with Lilia.

As she reached her apartment door, something yellow caught her eye. A sticky note.

Agatha frowned, fingers hovering over it before she peeled it off. The handwriting was unmistakable—bold, slanted, and messy.

Peeler please - R

She scoffed. Typical. No explanation. No pleasantries. Just Rio being... Rio.

For a moment, she debated ignoring it. Let Rio suffer the consequences of whatever culinary disaster she was attempting. But as she stood there, the note burning between her fingers, she felt an inexplicable tug of curiosity.

With a sigh, she stuffed the note into her pocket and unlocked her door. The apartment felt emptier than usual, the silence pressing in from all sides. She kicked off her shoes and wandered into the kitchen, absentmindedly rearranging the clutter on the counter. A misplaced coffee mug, a pile of unopened mail, a stray pen—anything to keep her hands busy while her thoughts kept circling back.

Rio. With her stupid note. And her stupid smirk. And the way she always managed to wedge herself into Agatha’s mind like an annoying, persistent song.

Agatha set down a stack of papers with a sharp thud.

Fine. She’d find the damn peeler.

-

A few hours later, Agatha stood outside Rio's door, the small kitchen tool in her hand. She had told herself this was just a simple errand—drop the peeler off, get it over with—but the longer she stood there, the more she realised she’d built this moment up in her head. The irritation buzzing in her veins wasn’t just about the note. It was everything—the smugness, the teasing, the sounds from last night.

She took a breath and knocked, a little too forcefully.

The door swung open before she could knock again, and there was Rio, standing in the frame. Effortlessly casual as always—loose t-shirt, pyjama pants (her own, for once)—but somehow still exuding that maddening confidence. Like she’d been expecting this. Like she knew exactly what she was doing.

Agatha blinked, thrown for a second. She had anticipated the usual arrogance, the smirk, the smart remark. But Rio just stood there, unreadable, and that was somehow even more disarming.

“You here to drop off my peeler?” Rio asked, voice steady, but with something lingering beneath it. Like she was waiting for Agatha to say something else.

Agatha blinked again, then quickly recovered, holding out the peeler with a sharp, clipped tone. “Here. And thanks so much for keeping it down last night,” she added, sarcasm dripping from her words.

Rio’s lips twitched, amusement sparking in her dark eyes. And then, just as Agatha thought she might let it slide, there it was—that smirk. Slow. Infuriating.

"You're welcome,” Rio drawled. “I know how thin our walls are, so I did try and get her to keep it down…"

Agatha’s grip tightened on the peeler as the words sank in. The casualness of it. The way Rio spoke so matter-of-factly, as if it wasn’t a big deal.

“You tried?” Agatha repeated, voice low with disbelief as her hand dropped back to her side and her grip on the peeler tightening in her fist. “You planned to be loud, didn’t you? And you just—” She cut herself off, jaw clenching. This was ridiculous. This conversation was ridiculous. But Rio’s steady gaze—calm, unwavering—pulled the words right out of her.

Rio leaned in just slightly, eyes nevr leaving Agatha’s. “I didn’t plan it,” she said, voice dropping just enough to make Agatha’s stomach twist. “But I’m not exactly sorry about it either.” A pause. Then, softer, more deliberate— “Though if I knew you were listening so intently, I would have been a bit more enthusiastic myself.”

Agatha exhaled sharply through her nose, heat creeping up her neck. Nope. Not doing this.

She turned on her heel, muttering a string of unintelligible curses under her breath.

“The peeler, Agatha,” Rio called after her, voice lazy, playful, infuriating. How many times can Agatha call this woman infuriating?

Agatha almost kept walking. Almost.

Grinding her teeth, she pivoted sharply, marching back toward Rio with stiff movements. She shoved the peeler into Rio’s waiting hand, her fingers barely grazing against Rio’s before she yanked them back like she’d been burned.

Rio accepted it slowly, deliberately, letting the moment stretch just long enough to be noticed. She met Agatha’s gaze, her smirk deepening. “Thanks,” she murmured, all smooth confidence.

Agatha’s heart thudded in her chest, pulse a little too fast. It was just a peeler, damn it. But Rio was looking at her like she knew—like she could see exactly what was happening in Agatha’s head, and worse, she was enjoying it.

Rio leaned against the doorframe, tilting her head slightly. “Bye, Agatha,” she said, soft but weighted. Like the words meant more than just goodbye.

Agatha stared at her for a second longer, her hand twitching at her side. Every instinct screamed at her to come up with a retort, something to wipe that smug look off Rio’s face. But nothing came.

She turned sharply on her heel. “Unbelievable,” she muttered, just loud enough for Rio to hear, before stalking back toward her apartment. She could feel Rio’s eyes on her, a presence that lingered even as she reached her door.

She slammed it shut behind her, pressing her back against the wood, exhaling slowly.

-

A week later, Agatha was exhausted. The workweek had dragged on, and she was more than ready to collapse on her couch with a cup of tea and a good book. She fumbled with her keys as she reached her apartment door, barely registering the familiar quiet of the hallway. It had been a hectic few days, and she was craving some peace and solitude.

When she opened the door, however, she froze.

There, sprawled out on her couch, was Rio. Of course it was Rio. The audacity of it.

“Are you serious?” Agatha blurted, stepping inside. Her bag slipped off her shoulder and thudded to the ground, but she didn’t bother to pick it up. Rio was lounging as though this was the most natural thing in the world, eyes fixed on the TV.

Rio turned lazily toward Agatha, a smirk already tugging at the corners of her mouth. “Evening, Agatha,” she said with casual nonchalance, like her presence was completely expected. “I hope you don’t mind. Thought I’d make myself comfortable.”

Agatha blinked, her jaw tightening in frustration. “You thought you’d make yourself comfortable?” She said slowly, crossing her arms, disbelief laced with irritation.

Rio patted the space next to her on the couch. “Come on, take a seat. I’m not here to cause trouble. We need to talk.”

“Talk about what?” Agatha asked, incredulous. “What is this? You’re creating a habit of breaking in lately. Should I be calling the cops?”

Rio raised an eyebrow. "That's no way to talk to someone who made you dinner." She pointed to the coffee table, where a plate of pasta sat, steam still rising from it.

Agatha blinked, the anger momentarily shifting to confusion. "Wait—what?"

"Sit," Rio said, her tone softening just a little. She leaned forward, picking up the plate and handing it to Agatha. It was still warm. How had she known Agatha would be home so late?

Agatha grumbled under her breath, finally accepting the plate and sitting down beside Rio—though she kept a healthy distance.

Rio’s gaze flickered back to the TV, her faint smile far less mocking than usual.

“What do you want?” Agatha asked, her frustration giving way to curiosity. “I mean, what’s the deal? Why are you here?”

"Eat first," Rio said, her voice low but steady. "Then we'll talk."

Agatha huffed but couldn’t ignore the mouth-watering smell of the pasta. Her stomach growled as if it was a paid actor. It looked delicious. She didn’t know whether she was more irritated or impressed. She’d seen Rio in her kitchen plenty of times before, but this? This was a different level of strange.

Agatha squinted at Rio, suddenly suspicious. “Did you poison this?”

Rio laughed, a snort escaping her. “Poison you? Why would I bother?”

“Oh, I don’t know. Maybe because you’re weird and can’t just have a normal conversation?” Agatha’s voice dripped with sarcasm.

Rio grinned, leaning back against the couch. “Fair. But no, I didn’t poison it.”

“Promise?”

“Promise,” Rio replied, her voice amused.

Agatha hesitated, glancing between the plate and Rio’s face. Finally, her curiosity won out. She took a bite.

-

After the last bite, Agatha set the empty plate down on the coffee table. "It was good," she muttered, almost reluctantly. She hadn’t expected to be impressed, but the food was delicious—complex, surprising. She wasn’t exactly one to dish out compliments, but this was a welcome surprise.

“Told you,” Rio said, a small smirk still twitching at the corners of her mouth. “I can cook.”

“Fine, you can cook,” Agatha conceded, sitting back. “But why?”

Rio sighed, scratching the back of her neck. The gesture was almost awkward, at odds with her usual relaxed demeanour. Her smirk faded, and she glanced down at the empty plate as if gathering her thoughts.

“Listen,” she said, her voice suddenly softer, lacking the usual cocky edge. “I’m sorry about the other day.”

Agatha blinked, caught off guard. She hadn’t expected an apology. “You’re sorry?”

“I went too far,” Rio continued, shifting a little. “I don’t even know what I was thinking. But I shouldn’t have made you uncomf-”

“It’s fine,” Agatha cut in, surprising herself. She hadn’t meant to interrupt, but there was something in Rio’s tone that made her pause. “I mean… you didn’t have to go through all this.” She gestured to the food. “You could’ve just, I don’t know, talked to me. Like a normal person.”

Rio’s eyes flicked up to meet Agatha’s, and she let out a low chuckle. “Yeah, you’re right. I’m not great at normal.”

Agatha snorted, leaning back against the couch, a little more at ease now. “Tell me something I don’t know.”

“Okay, smartass,” Rio retorted, a grin creeping back onto her face. “I’ll try not to be so… annoying.”

“Yeah, that,” Agatha said, her lips quirking upward. “But seriously, I’m not going to hold it against you.”

Rio shook her head, the humour fading from her expression. “Look, I am sorry. Truly.”

Agatha hesitated, studying her. It was strange seeing Rio this open—this vulnerable. And she was apologising. For real.

“Okay,” Agatha said softly, her voice more forgiving. “I mean… thanks. For the apology. And the food.”

“Sure,” Rio replied, her cocky grin returning. “So, have you thought about my invite?”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “To what? The Christmas party?”

“Mhm.” Rio nodded, her gaze flickering back to the TV screen, but her focus was still on Agatha. “Have you?”

Agatha bit her lip, considering. She’d thought about it more than a few times, but something had held her back. “You said your coworker was overly touchy, right?”

“Oh, yeah,” Rio groaned, rolling her eyes. “He’s… a lot. Not dangerous, but always way too close. Like, really close.”

“Right,” Agatha nodded slowly, piecing it together. “And you don’t like that.”

“Nope.” Rio popped the ‘p,’ her eyes twinkling. “That’s why I need someone who can send a very clear message.”

“So, what?” Agatha asked, raising an eyebrow. “I’m just supposed to pretend we’re dating or something?”

Rio’s eyebrows shot up, her lips curling into a half-smile. “I mean, that’s what they’ll assume, yeah.”

Agatha sighed, rubbing her temples. “And what exactly are we going to tell them?”

Rio tilted her head, studying her with an easy grin spreading across her face. “Oh, I’m sure we can come up with something.”

Agatha let out a long, slow exhale. “Fine. Whatever.”

Rio beamed. “Yay! You won’t regret it. We will have so much fun!”

Agatha looked at her with a flat expression. “Can you leave now?”

“Hm... no. I don’t feel like going home yet so you’re stuck with me for a bit.”

Agatha groaned and Rio rolled her eyes before speaking again, “Oh lighten up. Don’t act like I’m not the highlight of your day. Your week even. Or dare I say your life?” She let out a fake gasp and plopped back against the couch dramatically.

Agatha just rolled her eyes at her dramatics and tucked her legs underneath her.

Rio smirked at the shift, stretching her arms behind her head before shifting her attention to the remote. “Anyway, since I’m here, we might as well watch a movie. What’s your poison? Comedy, horror, rom-com?”

Agatha opened her mouth to respond, but before she could get a word out, Rio had already clicked on a thriller, the eerie music swelling as the opening credits rolled.

Agatha narrowed her eyes. "You just asked me so you could ignore my answer."

Rio shot her a dazzling grin. "Exactly. But, hey, you get the illusion of choice. That counts for something."

Agatha crossed her arms. "It absolutely does not."

Rio shrugged, getting comfortable. "Well, too late now. The movie already started. And, you know, if you get scared, you can always hold my hand. No judgment."

Agatha scoffed. "I would rather be murdered by Billy Loomis.”

Rio hummed. "Kinda dramatic, but I get it... who wouldn’t amiright?"

As the movie played, Rio made it her mission to be as obnoxious as possible. She gasped theatrically at obvious jump scares, leaned over to whisper ridiculous commentary in Agatha’s ear, and—on more than one occasion—casually draped her arm over the back of the couch, inching ever so slightly closer.

Agatha, to her credit, ignored most of it. But when Rio let out a particularly exaggerated yelp and grabbed her arm, she finally turned to glare at her.

"Rio."

"Yes, dear?"

Agatha sighed, exasperated. "Stop being a menace."

Rio grinned, clearly unapologetic. "I have no idea what you’re talking about."

Agatha shook her head, refocusing on the movie. "You’re lucky I haven’t smothered you with a pillow."

"You wouldn’t." Rio’s voice was full of confidence.

Agatha glanced at her. "Wouldn’t I?"

Rio just smirked, leaning in slightly. "Nope. You like me too much."

Agatha scoffed but didn’t move away. Rio chuckled, pleased with herself, and turned back to the screen and Agatha couldn’t help but watch her.

-

It had been a few days since their movie night, and Agatha still wasn’t sure what had convinced her to agree to the Christmas party. Sure, she wanted to help Rio out, but this felt extreme. She barely knew the woman—she was practically a stranger—and an infuriating one at that.

As Agatha sat in her living room scrolling through her phone, a loud knock echoed from her front door. The noise startled her so much she nearly dropped her phone. Who the hell could that be?

She rose to her feet, her annoyance growing, and strode over to the door. She swung it open to reveal Rio, standing there with a grin on her face, her hand poised to knock again.

“Evening, neighbour,” Rio said, lowering her arm.

“Rio,” Agatha replied, still taken aback. She crossed her arms, leaning against the doorframe. “Surprised you even knocked. What do you want?”

“I was in the neighbourhood,” Rio said with exaggerated dramatic flair. Agatha rolled her eyes.

“Right,” she said flatly. “What do you want?” she repeated.

“Don’t be like that, Aggie,” Rio teased, her grin widening. Agatha felt a flare of irritation at the nickname. “I just thought we could go over our story... maybe practice a little.”

Agatha’s eyebrows shot up, and Rio’s face twisted into an infuriatingly smug expression. “Practice? What, like roleplay? Absolutely not. We can wing it on the night.” She made to close the door, but Rio blocked it with her foot.

“Ow,” Rio winced. “Listen, you’re good at lying, right? But I’m not. So, let’s make a plan. Y’know, since we got distracted the other night before we could actually come up with anything.”

“You think I’m good at lying?” Agatha asked incredulously, ignoring the remark about the other night. She had tried to forget about it. Too casual. Too friendly. They weren’t friends.

“Yeah, you’re always acting so standoffish. You can’t possibly be that much of a bitch, so you must be covering something up,” Rio reasoned.

“Wow. Thanks.” Agatha’s voice dripped with sarcasm, and she had every reason to slam the door in her face.

“Anyway, how did we meet? You know, the basics,” Rio asked, pushing her way into Agatha’s apartment. Agatha sighed and closed the door, turning to find Rio already lounging on the couch.

“Why can’t we just say we’re neighbours? It’s the truth,” Agatha offered, heading for the kitchen to grab a glass of water. Rio groaned and followed her.

“Neighbours isn’t a good enough story,” Rio complained, leaning against the kitchen counter.

“Oh, sorry. I forgot how important storytelling is to you,” Agatha muttered, rolling her eyes.

“Okay, fine. If you want to keep it simple, we can say we met at a party or something,” Rio suggested with a shrug.

“I’m 38 and I don’t like parties. You think anyone’s going to buy that?” Agatha pointed out.

“Okay, fair.” Rio tapped her fingers on the counter. “What about online? It’s the modern way to meet, right?”

Agatha sighed and pinched the bridge of her nose. This was giving her a headache. “No, because we’re not actually dating.”

“So, you want people to think we met through a window or something? Because that’s the vibe you’re giving off,” Rio quipped.

“We’re not meeting in windows, and we’re not lying either,” Agatha shot back, her irritation growing. “I’m not good at making things up, so let’s just stick with the truth and improvise.”

Rio narrowed her eyes, clearly not thrilled with the idea. “Fine,” she said after a moment, sighing. “Let’s practice anyway. How are we going to make this convincing?”

Agatha groaned and dragged a hand through her hair. “Can’t we just go over it once we’re there? Like a quick run-through?”

Rio crossed her arms, expression turning stubborn. “How do I know you’ll be able to sell it?”

Agatha finished her glass of water and set it down in the sink, turning to face Rio. “You don’t,” she said bluntly.

“Exactly. So we should go over it. What are our boundaries?” Rio pressed, taking a step closer to Agatha.

“What are our—We’re not talking boundaries right now,” Agatha sputtered, feeling her face flush.

“Then how are we going to know what we’re okay with? We’re not going to get through this if we don’t communicate,” Rio reasoned, her tone laced with sarcasm.

Agatha clenched her jaw, frustration rising. “Fine. You want to talk boundaries? Let’s talk boundaries.”

“Perfect,” Rio said, her tone shifting to serious. “Are you okay with me touching you? Holding hands, an arm around your waist, that kind of thing?”

“I mean… yes, that’s fine. If it’s necessary,” Agatha replied, trying to sound calm.

“Okay, good. How about kissing? Because if we’re going to sell this, I think we’ll need to—”

“Kissing?” Agatha blurted, her heart skipping a beat. “Like, on the lips?”

“Yeah, on the lips. Do you not know how kissing works? Because I can show—”

“I know how kissing works, thank you,” Agatha snapped, her face burning. She gripped the kitchen counter, trying to steady herself. “But kissing isn’t necessary, right? I mean, we’re not actually dating. We can just hold hands and stuff.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, a smirk pulling at her lips. “You think holding hands is going to be enough?”

“Yes,” Agatha replied firmly. “PDA isn’t necessary to sell a relationship.”

Rio studied her for a moment, a smirk still tugging at the corner of her mouth. “If you say so,” she said, sounding unconvinced. “Is there anywhere I’m not allowed to touch you?”

Agatha took a deep breath, willing herself to stay calm. “Anywhere you wouldn’t touch me as a friend.”

“Okay, that’s fair,” Rio said, seeming satisfied.

“Great,” Agatha replied, her tone clipped. She was starting to feel overwhelmed. She could handle touching, holding hands, but the thought of kissing was making her anxious. Was it because she was straight? Or was it just the idea of kissing Rio?

She refocused, meeting Rio’s gaze. The cocky grin was back on her face, the one that always made Agatha want to punch her. “So, you can leave now. I’m going to bed.”

“It’s 9 PM,” Rio pointed out, tilting her head slightly.

“Yeah, I’m tired. You wore me out,” Agatha shot back, turning and walking toward the front door to show Rio out.

“Oh, I’m sure I could wear you out some more,” Rio teased, following her.

Agatha didn’t give her the satisfaction of a reaction and simply opened the door.

“Goodnight,” Agatha said curtly, expression neutral.

Rio chuckled as she stepped outside. “See you Saturday, Aggie,” she called over her shoulder with a wink.

Chapter Four

The Christmas party was at a mini-golf course, and Agatha couldn’t decide what was more ridiculous—the concept itself or the fact that she was actually here, playing along with Rio’s insane scheme. The place was adorned with the most aggressively festive decorations she’d ever seen. Fairy lights clung to the course like ivy, oversized candy canes blocked the way as obstacles, and a giant inflatable Santa loomed by the entrance, its beady eyes unnervingly following her as she passed.

Rio, naturally, was in her element. She had thrown on a garish Christmas sweater featuring a winking reindeer, and her grin hadn’t wavered since they arrived. Agatha, on the other hand, was hyper-aware that she was about to spend the next few hours pretending to be Rio’s girlfriend in front of a crowd of strangers.

As they made their way toward the group of colleagues, Agatha paused, suddenly realising something. “Wait,” she said, narrowing her eyes at Rio. “I don’t even know what you do for work.”

Rio nearly choked on her laughter. “Aggie, we’ve been fake dating for five minutes and you’re already questioning my employment status?”

“Yes,” Agatha deadpanned. “It seems like a pretty fundamental detail, seeing as this is your work party.”

“I work in marketing,” Rio answered with a grin, “social media and branding, mostly. Explains why I’m so charming.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Charming? Not the word I'd use, but okay.”

Before Rio could reply, Agatha noticed a figure looming at the edge of the crowd—a tall, broad-shouldered man, standing just a little too still. His presence felt too familiar, the type of guy she’d met a hundred times before, with a smirk that made her want to avoid him at all costs. This had to be the touchy coworker Rio had warned her about. Of course, he was the first one to approach them.

“Hey, Rio,” he greeted, briefly glancing at Agatha before turning his attention back to Rio, a look that made Agatha’s skin crawl. “This must be the mysterious girlfriend. We were all wondering if she were real.” His eyes lingered on Rio, never once fully meeting Agatha's gaze, and Agatha fought the urge to punch him in the face.

She felt Rio shift closer, her hand slipping naturally into Agatha’s. “Yep,” Rio said easily, her voice light and confident. “This is Agatha. Agatha, this is Steve.” She gave Agatha’s hand a quick, reassuring squeeze, and Agatha’s heart skipped a beat. This was going to be a long night.

Steve extended his hand, and Agatha reluctantly pulled hers from Rio’s, briefly shaking his hand. His grip was too firm, lingering a fraction longer than necessary. Agatha fought the urge to yank her hand back with force, instead pulling it slowly, deliberately, wrapping it around Rio’s waist as if to stake her claim. Rio didn’t seem surprised by the gesture, though Agatha felt her press a little more firmly against her side, her arm sliding around her waist in return. The awkward silence between them seemed to stretch, Steve’s eyes flicking down to where their bodies connected.

“So... she’s real, huh?” Steve mused, his tone teasing, but there was an edge of skepticism that grated on Agatha’s nerves. Why wouldn’t this jerk just walk away already? He was blocking the entrance. “Guess that ruins my theory.”

“What theory?” Agatha asked, her voice sharp as she tilted her head. She caught Rio’s subtle groan beside her, too quiet for Steve to hear.

“That Rio just made up a fake girlfriend to keep me at bay.”

Agatha barely stopped herself from grimacing. She could already see why Rio needed backup. “Well,” she said, forcing a smile, “I am very real. Maybe you should learn to take no for an answer, whether or not the person you’re interested in is in a relationship.”

She felt Rio stiffen beside her, surprise flickering in her expression, but it quickly morphed into a small, amused smile. Agatha wasn’t sure if it was because of her response or something else, but she couldn’t help but feel a small surge of satisfaction at the reaction.

Steve’s smirk faltered, his mouth opening as if to respond—but before he could, a new voice cut through the conversation.

“There you are! Oh my god, Rio, you didn’t tell me she was this gorgeous.”

The new woman’s voice was warm and full of enthusiasm. She had an edgy vibe, with black hair cascading over her shoulders and orange-tipped ends that caught the light as she moved. Her smile was wide and inviting as she walked toward them with her arms spread out, clearly expecting a hug or some other show of affection. Agatha immediately felt her cheeks heat, the compliment making her awkward. Rio’s hand squeezed her side as she gave the woman a small side hug with her spare arm, and Agatha flinched, feeling her heartbeat jump at the touch.

Steve, seemingly annoyed by the interruption, cleared his throat. His gaze shifted away from Rio for the first time since he’d approached them. “Alright, well, I guess I should go find the others,” he muttered, obviously eager to escape. “See you around, Rio. Nice to meet you, Agatha. Sorry if I came off as too forward. Didn’t mean anything by it. You know how it is around Christmas time. People get a little wild, flirtatious, and all that. Hope you enjoy the party, ladies. Let me know if you need anything. Anything at all, Rio. I’m here for you, okay? Bye-bye now. Have a good evening.”

Agatha stood there, her teeth clenched as Steve rambled. Seriously, this guy was like a broken record. The urge to throttle him was almost overwhelming. Okay, maybe that’s a bit extreme, she thought to herself, but not by much.

Once Steve had disappeared back into the throng of partygoers, the newcomer turned to Rio, her eyebrows raised in curiosity. “Did I interrupt something?” she asked, her eyes wide in playful amusement.

Rio waved her hand dismissively. “Nah, you were saving us, honestly. He was just being weird again.” She glanced at Agatha, her grin widening. “Aggie, this is my friend Alice. She’s in my department and, well, she knows the whole story about why I brought you tonight.”

Alice gave Agatha a knowing smile, her eyes sparkling as she took in her appearance. “She failed to mention how stunning you are, though. I’m so glad you’re here to help her with Steve. He’s honestly one move away from being reported.” Alice's voice was laced with a mischievous energy that instantly put Agatha at ease, her earlier awkwardness softening a little.

As Alice spoke, Agatha became acutely aware of the way her arm was still wrapped around Rio—tightly. Her hand rested on Rio's hip, and Rio, it seemed, was leaning into her slightly, as if they were already comfortable in each other's space. It took Agatha a moment to process, but once she did, the heat in her face flared up again. Oh God. What am I doing?

Clearing her throat, Agatha slowly unwrapped her arm from around Rio’s waist. The loss of Rio’s warmth was almost immediate, and she couldn’t help but feel a little disappointed. She quickly tried to brush off the feeling, mumbling, “Sorry,” hoping her face wasn’t too red. The last thing she needed was Rio teasing her about it later.

Rio flashed her an easy smile, stepping back slightly, though her eyes held a glimmer of something that Agatha couldn’t quite place. “It’s fine,” she said, though Agatha noticed the brief flicker of hesitation before Rio dropped her hand from Agatha’s waist. A part of Agatha wished she’d pull her back, but she didn’t want to think about why that was.

Shifting uncomfortably, Agatha glanced up at Alice, who was watching her with an amused expression. “Uh, thanks,” she replied quickly, her voice awkward as she tried to gather her thoughts. “I’m happy to help.” She wasn’t sure how to respond, not knowing whether she was trying to convince Alice or herself.

Alice’s grin widened as her eyes danced between Agatha and Rio. “I’ll leave you to the course, then,” she said, her voice light with humour. “Don’t worry, the drinks are free. Enjoy!” She winked playfully at Agatha, who felt her face burn even hotter.

“Thanks,” Agatha muttered, trying to hide her red face behind her hair as Alice made her way off toward the rest of the party.

Rio’s gaze lingered on Agatha for a beat longer than was necessary, but when she spoke, her voice was casual. “You okay?” she asked, her tone soft with something almost teasing beneath it.

Agatha nodded quickly, though her heart was still thudding in her chest. “Yeah, just… just peachy,” she said, giving Rio a half-smile, trying to recover her usual composure.

Rio smirked. “Well then, are you ready to play mini-golf, fake girlfriend?”

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “I don’t really play sports.”

Rio gasped dramatically. “You wound me.”

“But” Agatha continued, ignoring her, “I’m willing to try anything once, I guess.”

Rio’s smirk deepened, and she arched an eyebrow. “Anything?”

Agatha’s heart did an entirely unnecessary thump. There she was. The Rio who thrived on making her flustered. She cleared her throat and pointedly ignored the comment, scanning the course like it was suddenly the most interesting thing in the world.

Rio laughed, clearly pleased with herself, and took Agatha’s hand, tugging her toward the golf clubs. The casual touch shouldn’t have sent a jolt of warmth up Agatha’s arm, but it did, and she had no idea what to do with that.

“It’s barely a sport, Agatha,” Rio teased, selecting two clubs and handing one over. “Don’t worry, I’ll go easy on you.”

Agatha scoffed, gripping the club tightly and ignoring the way her palm still tingled from Rio’s touch. “Don’t hold back on my account.”

Rio’s eyes gleamed with something dangerous. “You might regret saying that.”

She grabbed a pink ball for herself and handed Agatha a blue one before nodding toward the start of the course. “Shall we?”

“Lead the way,” Agatha agreed, falling into step beside her.

In her head, she was already strategizing. She had never played mini golf before, but she was not about to lose. She was 38, and she had a competitive streak that had ended friendships before. She would win.

Rio set her ball down first, stretching her arms dramatically like she was about to do something impressive. “Okay, so,” she began, “first rule of mini-golf is—there are no rules.”

Agatha frowned. “That doesn’t sound right.”

Rio ignored her. “Second rule—” she continued, lining up her shot, “aim for the hole.”

Agatha stared at her. “Obviously.”

Ignored again.

“Third rule—”

“How many rules are there? Didn’t you just say there were no rules?”

Rio turned her head slowly, raising a single warning eyebrow. “Third rule is don’t interrupt the master.”

Agatha bit back a smirk, rolling her eyes. “Oh, master, is it?”

“Yes. The Mini-Golf Master.”

“Oh my god.”

Rio grinned and continued. “And fourth rule…” She paused, tapping her chin with the club. “Nope, I think that’s it.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “You just made all that up.”

Rio’s smirk widened. “Maybe.”

Agatha sighed. “Are you going to hit the ball anytime soon?”

“Patience,” Rio chided, turning her focus back to the course. She squared her stance, squinted as if she were calculating the perfect shot, then pulled back and swung. The club connected with the ball with a soft thwack, sending it rolling neatly across the green, veering slightly left—before dropping directly into the hole.

Agatha blinked. What.

Rio spun on her heel, eyes alight with amusement. “Not bad, huh?”

Agatha crossed her arms. “Whatever.”

Rio chuckled, stepping aside as Agatha moved into place. “Let’s see what you’ve got, then.”

Agatha set her ball down, gripping her club tightly. She lined up her shot, adjusted her stance like she’d seen Rio do, and swung.

She immediately regretted her confidence.

The ball ricocheted off the edge of the hole, bounced backward, and rolled to a stop a solid three feet from where it started.
