Rio’s laughter rang through the air, bright and teasing.

Agatha clenched her jaw and turned away. “It was my first try,” she huffed.

“I know,” Rio said, her voice full of faux sympathy. “I just expected a little more…” She trailed off, as if searching for the right word. “Competence.”

Agatha shot her a glare. “I hope you fall into the water feature.”

Rio beamed. “Aw, you’re so sweet to me.”

Agatha tried to stay annoyed, but it was getting increasingly difficult. Especially when Rio was standing there, looking at her with that damn smirk, her dimples deepening, her eyes catching the glow of the fairy lights like something out of a Christmas movie.

Agatha swallowed.

After three more tries—each more humiliating than the last—Rio finally took pity on her. Or, more likely, she saw another opportunity to be insufferable.

Agatha had just lined up her shot again when she felt Rio step in behind her, impossibly close, her hands sliding over Agatha’s own.

"Like this," Rio murmured, voice low and smug, guiding Agatha’s hands with featherlight touches.

Agatha stiffened. Nope. Absolutely not.

"I'm not sure that's gonna help," she muttered, trying to focus on the club and not the fact that Rio’s front was now pressed up against her back, warm and solid. She could feel the shape of her, the way she fit against her like a puzzle piece she definitely didn’t need to be thinking about right now.

Rio laughed, her breath brushing the back of Agatha's neck, sending an involuntary shiver down her spine. "Oh, Aggie," she teased, her fingers flexing slightly over Agatha’s. "Have a little faith."

Agatha had none.

None in Rio. None in this ridiculous game. None in herself, because her pulse was behaving in a way that was both unacceptable and entirely predictable.

And then—Rio stepped away, her hands trailing off Agatha’s in a way that felt far too intentional. Damn her.

"Try it," Rio urged, like she hadn’t just ruined every ounce of Agatha’s ability to function.

Agatha scowled, repeating mockingly, “Try it.” Then, louder, "I will," and took her shot.

The ball sailed right past the hole, bouncing off the edge and rolling away like it had personally decided to embarrass her.

Rio burst into laughter, full and delighted, shaking her head. "Aggie."

Agatha gritted her teeth. "That was your fault."

"Oh?" Rio arched an eyebrow, taking a step towards her, "My fault?"

"Yes," Agatha snapped, resisting the urge to fling her club into the nearest decorative Santa.

"Interesting," Rio mused. "Because I distinctly remember you taking the shot."

Agatha turned to glare at her, but Rio was already grinning, smug and infuriating, and—oh, for the love of—

Rio reached out and flicked Agatha’s nose.

Agatha jerked back, scandalised. “Did you just—”

"You're so cute when you're flustered," Rio said breezily, twirling her club like she was twirling a villainous moustache. "It’s almost a shame you’re so bad at this."

Agatha inhaled sharply. She would not kill her. This was a work event. There were witnesses.

"You are the worst person I have ever met," she hissed, willing her face not to turn any redder.

Rio pouted, unbothered. "That can't be true. I’m delightful."

Agatha exhaled sharply through her nose and turned back to the course, gripping her club a little too tightly.

"Would it help if I promised not to tease you too much if you make this next shot?" Rio asked, tone full of mischief.

Agatha refused to dignify that with a response.

They made it through three more holes—Agatha getting increasingly frustrated, Rio getting increasingly insufferable—before Agatha called for a break.

"Drinks," she announced, cutting off Rio mid-taunt as she waved toward the little concession stand near the course. "If I have to keep playing, I need a drink first."

Rio gasped, pressing a hand to her chest in mock horror. "Giving up already?"

Agatha narrowed her eyes. "I am strategising."

"Ah," Rio said, nodding perceptively. "The classic ‘get tipsy and somehow become a mini-golf prodigy’ technique. Bold."

"Are you going to let me drink in peace, or do I have to push you into one of these giant candy canes?"

Rio grinned. "Oh, by all means, push me, Aggie. I love being manhandled."

Agatha exhaled sharply and stomped toward the bar, pointedly ignoring Rio’s laughter behind her.

The concession stand was a gaudy little setup, strung with blinking multi-coloured lights that looked like they might give someone a seizure. The menu offered a selection of overly sweet holiday-themed cocktails, along with beer, wine, and a tragic attempt at a hot chocolate station.

Rio leaned against the counter, scanning the options. "What'll it be, fake girlfriend?"

"Anything with alcohol," Agatha said. "A lot of alcohol."

Rio turned to the bartender. "She'll have a mulled wine. I'll take a spiked eggnog, extra whipped cream."

Agatha gave her a look. "Do you just want the excuse to lick it off the top dramatically?"

Rio gasped, delighted. "Oh my god, you do know me."

Agatha groaned and turned away, eyes landing on a group of Rio’s coworkers gathered near one of the high tables. Unfortunately, before she could even attempt to drink in peace, Rio spotted them too.

"Oh, hey, we should probably go say hi."

Agatha stared at her. "Must we?"

"Yes, we must." Rio grabbed her by the sleeve and tugged her toward the group, ignoring Agatha’s whispered threats of bodily harm.

"Everyone, this is Agatha," Rio announced grandly as they reached the table. "My lovely, talented, very real girlfriend."

Agatha barely resisted the urge to bury her face in her hands.

The group greeted her with various degrees of warmth and curiosity, some clearly amused by the whole charade, others just happy to put a name to Rio’s mysterious plus-one. Alice was there, shooting Agatha a knowing smirk, and a few other people introduced themselves between sips of their drinks.

"So, Aggie," a tall, wiry guy named Billy said, leaning on the table, "how’d Rio rope you into this?"

Before Agatha could answer, Rio clutched at her chest dramatically. "Rope? Rope? Excuse me, Billy, but Agatha is madly in love with me."

Agatha blinked, startled. "I—"

"It’s tragic, really," Rio continued, undeterred. "She’s completely helpless against my charm. She saw me once and immediately swooned."

Alice snorted into her drink. "That does not sound like Agatha." Jeez, how much had Rio told Alice about her?

"It isn't," Agatha said flatly, shooting Rio a glare.

"Oh, come on," Rio whined, nudging her. "Just pretend I swept you off your feet, Aggie."

Agatha took a slow sip of her wine, considering her options. Then, in the driest tone possible, she said, “Fine. She swept me off my feet. Unfortunately, I must have blacked out from the impact, because I woke up and somehow, we were dating.”

The group erupted into laughter, and Rio, the absolute menace that she was, leaned in close, her voice low and teasing. “Oh, thank you for playing along, Aggie. I’ll make sure to reward you later.”

Agatha nearly choked on her drink.

She shot Rio a withering look, but Rio just grinned, clearly enjoying how flustered Agatha had become. She was about to retaliate when she noticed something odd—Steve, standing just a little outside the group, suddenly very interested in his drink. He hadn’t said a word since they arrived, and more importantly, he was pointedly avoiding looking at them.

That was… surprising.

Agatha expected him to interject, to make some snide remark, or at the very least, keep up whatever annoying bravado he had going earlier. But instead, he seemed to have shrunk into himself, his eyes flicking anywhere but at her and Rio.

Interesting.

She glanced at Rio, who was too busy grinning at something Alice had said to notice. Maybe Steve had finally gotten the message. Maybe her earlier remark had hit harder than she thought.

Or maybe, just maybe, he was recalibrating—trying to find another angle, another way to push Rio’s buttons.

Agatha didn’t trust it.

She leaned in slightly toward Rio and murmured, “Steve’s awfully quiet all of a sudden.”

Rio blinked, then subtly turned her head toward him before looking back at Agatha, her brow lifting. “Huh. He is.”

“I don’t like it.”

Rio smirked. “You do care about me.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I just don’t trust him.”

"Relax, babe," Rio teased, purposefully draping an arm around Agatha’s waist and whispered. "That’s why I have you here with me."

Agatha sighed, willing herself not to react to the casual touch. "Just… keep an eye on him."

Rio's smirk softened into something almost thoughtful. "I always do."

The night wore on in a blur of drinks, laughter, and forced smiles. Agatha couldn’t remember the last time she’d attended a party quite like this—pretending to be someone’s girlfriend in front of a group of strangers, with Rio constantly by her side. Every time Agatha felt herself pull away, Rio seemed to close the distance, her touch always a little too warm, her presence a little too close.

The constant physical contact was starting to blur the lines. Rio had her arm around her waist, had tucked herself under Agatha’s shoulder more than once, and each time, Agatha found herself not pulling away. In fact, she was starting to feel a strange, almost reluctant comfort in it. When Rio leaned against her, her hand brushing just a little too low on her back or her fingers grazing her arm, Agatha’s pulse would race for a split second before she reminded herself—it’s just for the act.

But the thing was, it didn’t feel like just an act anymore. Not when Rio’s fingers lingered a little too long on her skin, or when she caught Agatha’s eye with that teasing, almost flirtatious glint. It made her stomach do little flips, like Rio was playing a game she didn’t know the rules to.

By the time the evening started winding down, Agatha was ready to call it quits. The evening had stretched longer than she'd expected, her forced smiles starting to feel more like actual strain. She was exhausted—physically from the constant movement and mentally from the underlying tension, trying to stay focused while pretending that the little electric touches from Rio didn’t make her skin hum in ways it shouldn’t.

Rio was still floating around, effortlessly charming everyone and holding court with her colleagues. Agatha had long since lost track of time, but she found herself counting the minutes until she could finally escape to the quiet of her own space.

She glanced at the clock on the wall. Definitely time to go. She shifted uncomfortably, trying to ignore the fact that Rio’s hand had somehow found its way back to her waist again.

"Okay, this has been fun and all," Agatha said, trying to inject some finality into her voice, though it came out a little softer than she'd intended. "But I think it’s time to wrap it up, don’t you think?"

Rio’s arm tightened slightly around her, not in a way that felt possessive, but more like an invitation to stay longer, like she didn’t want the night to end. Agatha tried to ignore the way it made her stomach flip again.

“Already?” Rio asked, her voice laced with playful disbelief, as if she was genuinely enjoying herself. She lowered her voice and lent in as she said, “I thought you were having fun pretending to be my girlfriend, Aggie.”

Agatha had long ago stopped drinking, as she had to drive them home, but Rio’s proximity made her head swim, nonetheless. But she could say the opposite for Rio.

"Believe me, I’m all for playing pretend, but I think I’ve paid you back thoroughly and have earned a good night’s sleep," Agatha replied dryly, though there was a hint of softness to it.

Rio’s eyes softened too, just for a second, before she winked. “I think you’ve earned a lot more than that. You’ve been the perfect date.”

Agatha fought the urge to roll her eyes. “I’m sure I’ve been a delight to everyone here, but I’m still ready to go home.”

“Mm, alright. But I’ll let you in on a little secret,” Rio said, voice lowering like she was sharing some sort of confidant’s whisper. She leaned in just a little closer, her lips brushing the shell of Agatha’s ear. “I’ll miss having you this close, Aggie.”

Agatha froze for a second, not sure if the words were playful or if there was something else behind them. She quickly pushed the thought away. It’s just part of the act. Just a game.

“I’m sure you will,” Agatha muttered, trying to shrug off the fluttering sensation in her chest. She smiled, but it felt more forced than the ones she’d been giving all night. She was finding it increasingly harder to remind herself she was straight and that this meant nothing.

Rio pulled back, an unreadable look flashing in her eyes before her grin returned, all charm. “Alright, alright. Let’s get out of here then.”

They said their goodbyes before they began walking toward the exit. Agatha found herself deliberately not looking at Rio, focusing instead on her shoes or the path ahead. She was too tired to deal with whatever this night had stirred up. Just get through the door and you’ll be fine, she thought. Just keep reminding yourself—it’s an act.

The moans were softer now, more erratic.

Agatha clenched her fists.

She shouldn’t still be listening, shouldn’t be hyper-focused on the final, breathy whimper that sent a fresh wave of warmth through her.

Then silence.

She exhaled, long and shaky.

It was over.

Agatha let out a breathy, almost disbelieving laugh at herself. She had been seconds—seconds—away from doing something she’d never be able to come back from.

This was Rio, her annoying, infuriating neighbour.

This was not supposed to happen.

Swallowing hard, she forced herself to lie back down, rolling onto her side and yanking the blanket over her body like it could smother out everything she was feeling.

She squeezed her eyes shut.

It was just the act getting to her. That was all.

She was touch-starved, that was it.

It didn’t mean anything.

It couldn’t.

But as she lay there, staring at the wall that separated them, her body still humming with unwanted heat, she couldn’t ignore the truth clawing its way to the surface.

She had never been curious about women before.

So why did she suddenly feel like she was one bad decision away from knocking on Rio’s door?

Chapter Five

Agatha’s grip on her keys tightened. The invitation—so casual, so easy—sent a ripple of unease through her. She opened her mouth, ready to decline on instinct, to come up with some excuse about work or an early morning, but nothing came out.

Because the way Rio was looking at her—sharp, amused, expectant—made her pulse stutter.

Rio hummed, tilting her head just slightly. “Busy?”

“Yes.”

“With what?”

Agatha faltered. She hadn’t prepared for a follow-up. “Things.”

Rio’s smirk deepened. “Oh, things.”

God, she was irritating.

Agatha turned back to her door, slipping her key into the lock, but her hand felt unsteady. She hated that. Hated that Rio could rattle her without even trying. And worst of all, she hated how the moment she looked at her—really looked—something in her chest went tight.

Because she hadn’t seen her in days. And it shouldn’t have mattered. But it did.

But she wasn’t going to crack.

For a second, Rio almost looked surprised. Then her grin widened, all teeth, all satisfaction.

Still watching her.

Immediately.

“I thought if I gave you space—rules—you’d feel safer. You’d stay. I thought maybe if I waited long enough, you’d stop pretending this didn’t matter.”

Agatha couldn’t speak. Couldn’t move. Could only sit there, spine rigid, heart kicking against her ribs like it was trying to escape.

“I’ve been trying,” Rio went on, eyes shining. “To meet you where you are. To make this work on your terms. But every time I think we’re getting somewhere, you run.”

“I’m not—” Agatha tried, but the words collapsed in her throat.

“Yes, you are.” Rio’s voice was sharp now. “You push me out. You shut me out. And I keep telling myself it’s okay, that you just need time, but—fuck, Agatha, I’m tired of talking to a locked door.”

Agatha looked down at her hands. “I’m sorry,” she whispered.

Rio laughed bitterly. “You’re not. You’re scared. And instead of saying that, you just light a match and act surprised when it burns.”

Agatha didn’t respond.

Because she couldn’t deny it.

Rio stood suddenly, the air shifting. She dragged her shirt on like armour, her movements tight and fast. Like if she stayed still too long, she might break.

“You don’t get to play the victim in this,” she said, voice low and shaking. “I made the rules, yeah—but only because I didn’t think you’d stay without them.”

“I didn’t mean for it to get messy,” Agatha whispered.

Rio looked at her then—really looked at her, and the crack in her expression was almost too much to bear. “It was always messy. You just didn’t want to admit it.”

Silence thickened between them.

Agatha stared at the floor, nails digging into her thighs. She couldn’t look up. Couldn’t risk seeing how much damage she’d done.

“I should go,” Rio murmured.

She stepped toward the door. Each movement soft, slow. Like she was waiting for something.

A word. A reason to stay.

Agatha stayed quiet.

But Rio didn’t leave.

She exhaled—sharp, frustrated. Her hand clenched at her side.
“You know what pisses me off the most?” she said, turning back. “It’s not that you’re ending it. It’s that you’re pretending it never mattered.”

Agatha’s jaw locked.
“I never said that.”

“No,” Rio said, voice cracking. “But you’re acting like it. Like none of it meant anything. Like I didn’t.”

“That’s not—” Agatha stood, too fast, regretting it instantly. Now they were eye to eye. Close enough to hurt each other properly.

Rio’s eyes were glassy with fury she hadn’t bothered to swallow. “You think you’re being noble? Responsible? Fine. Good for you. But I wanted this. You. Even when you made it impossible. Even when you gave me nothing.”

“You don’t understand,” Agatha said, voice thinner than she meant.

“I understand perfectly,” Rio snapped. “You keep throwing my age in my face like it’s some kind of trap I walked into blind. Like I didn’t know what I was doing.” She stepped forward. “I chose you. Not because it was easy. Because it wasn’t.”

“You think this was casual?” Rio’s laugh was hollow. “You think I kept showing up, kept letting you shut me out, kept trying, just for the sex?”

Agatha flinched.

Rio’s voice dropped to something raw, something almost broken. “I want you, Agatha. Not just in your bed. In your life. For real. And I’m so fucking tired of pretending I don’t.”

Silence.

Agatha’s lip trembled. She looked down. “I don’t know how to do this.”

Rio didn’t back away. “Then say that. Be fucking honest. Say you’re scared. Say you’re overwhelmed. But don’t rewrite what we had just because it hurts.”

Agatha’s mouth opened. Nothing came out.

Rio shook her head once. Then:
“You want me to leave?” Her voice barely held. “Say it. Look at me and say it meant nothing. That I meant nothing. And I swear, I’ll walk out that door and never come back.”

Agatha’s breath hitched.
Her mouth opened—but nothing came out.

She looked at Rio. Really looked.
Hair a mess. Eyes glassy. Shoulders squared like she was trying to hold her own heart in place.

Say it.
Say it meant nothing.
Say it and be done with it.

Her jaw tightened. Her throat worked around the words. But they wouldn’t form.

Because they weren’t true.

And even if she wanted to lie—wanted to protect herself the way she always did—something in Rio’s face made it impossible.

“I can’t,” Agatha whispered, voice cracking.

Her body stilled in that awful, brittle way—like glass under pressure. One wrong breath and she’d crack down the middle.

Rio was still there. Not touching her. Not demanding anything. Just standing in it. In the mess. In the silence. In the wreckage of everything Agatha had tried to hold back.

And Agatha couldn’t look at her.
Because if she did, if she let her eyes meet Rio’s—she’d lose the last thread holding her upright. She could feel it already. The sting behind her eyes. The tremble in her ribs.

But Rio didn’t move away.
Didn’t leave.
Didn’t shout.

She stepped forward slowly. Steady. Deliberate.
And lifted her hand.

Agatha’s heart jumped. She flinched—just a flicker, not even a full motion—but Rio saw it. She always saw it. And still, her hand kept coming.

A soft, steady palm against her cheek. Barely there.

Agatha still didn’t look up.

Then—Rio’s thumb brushed under her eye.

That’s when Agatha felt it.
Wet.
Hot.

She hadn’t noticed. Hadn’t realised. But her cheeks were already damp.

She blinked. Another tear spilled.

Rio caught it.
Said nothing.

Just wiped it away like it wasn’t shocking. Like it wasn’t a crisis. Like she’d expected it—like she knew.

Agatha’s throat squeezed tight.
Her hands stayed clenched at her sides.

She was naked. Not just physically—though that hit her too. She was completely exposed. No excuses. No control. Just a raw, shivering thing standing in the middle of her own fears.

Then Rio’s other hand came up.
Joined the first.

She cupped Agatha’s face in both palms, like she was holding something breakable. Something holy.

Agatha still didn’t look at her.
Couldn’t.

The pressure in her chest built like a scream behind a locked door.

She didn’t know what this was—this tenderness. This quiet. This mercy in the face of rejection. But it was unbearable. It was cracking her open.

And Rio just held her.
Didn’t force her to speak.
Didn’t let her go.

The dam broke.

Agatha’s face crumpled.

It wasn’t a sob at first. Just a sound—small, torn from the back of her throat. Her shoulders curled in. Her whole body folded like she’d been struck.

Rio caught her.

Arms around her in an instant. One hand still on her cheek, the other behind her neck. Holding her steady. Holding her here.

Agatha pressed her face to Rio’s shoulder and finally let herself cry.

It was ugly. Shaking. Gasping. Like her body had forgotten how to fall apart properly. Years of tight-lipped control shredded in seconds—spilling onto bare skin and warm breath and the chest of the girl who refused to leave.

“I’m sorry,” Agatha choked against her neck, though she didn’t even know what for. “I’m sorry, I just—fuck—”

Rio didn’t hush her.
Didn’t say it was okay.
She just held her tighter. Let her shatter. Let her bleed it all out without flinching.

Like she wanted this.
Like she needed Agatha to stop pretending she didn’t feel it too.

And in that moment—that awful, silent, shaking moment—Agatha knew:
It was too late to go back.

Because this wasn’t casual.
Had never been casual.
Not for a second.

Her knees buckled. She didn’t even notice until Rio caught her. Again.

Like it was nothing.
Like she’d been ready.

She lowered them to the edge of the bed with terrifying gentleness. The kind that only made Agatha cry harder. The kind that made it real.

She couldn’t breathe. Not through the guilt. Not through the sobs. Her ribs stuttered, lungs collapsing like paper in the rain.

“I’m sorry,” she whispered again, barely there.

Rio didn’t speak.
Just pressed her forehead to Agatha’s temple. One hand splayed over her spine. The other still cupping her jaw like it was the only thing tethering her to the earth.

Agatha let herself be held.

Because she didn’t know how to ask for this. Not out loud.
Didn’t know how to say please stay without sounding desperate, or I’m scared without sounding ungrateful.
Didn’t know how to say I want you without feeling like a liar.

So she just curled in, raw and bare, until the sobs dulled. Until the storm passed.
Until all that remained was the soft, shuddering ache of aftermath—like she was a door someone had kicked in, hinges still swinging.

“I didn’t mean for it to be like this,” she said eventually, voice hoarse. “I didn’t mean to hurt you.”

Rio shifted. Just enough to look at her.

“Then why did you?” she asked. Not angry. Just... empty. Hollowed out and trying to understand. “Why do you keep pushing me away like I haven’t already seen the worst of you?”

Agatha’s throat clicked. She looked down.

“Because if I let myself want this,” she said quietly, “and it goes wrong…”

Rio waited.

Agatha swallowed. “I don’t know if I’ll come back from it.”

There it was.
The truth, bleeding out of her like a wound that had waited years to open.

She met Rio’s eyes. Finally.

And hated what she saw.
Not pity. Not triumph.
Just that quiet, devastating look that said me too.

Rio reached up. Brushed the damp hair from Agatha’s forehead.

“I want this,” she said. Simple. Steady. Fierce. “I want you, Agatha. For real.”

Agatha blinked. A fresh tear slipped free.

“But if you keep pretending you don’t care…” Rio’s voice cracked. “I’ll start to believe you. And if that happens—I will walk away.”

It wasn’t a threat.
It was a truth.
A line drawn gently, but unmistakably, in the sand.

“I do care,” Agatha whispered. “I just… I don’t know how to do this.”

Rio exhaled—half a laugh, half a sigh. “Neither do I.”

Silence bloomed. Not empty. Heavy. Alive.

Agatha’s hand moved without thinking, fingers curling into the hem of Rio’s shirt like she needed something—someone—to hold onto.

Rio looked down at it. Then back at her.

“Can I stay?” she asked.
No games. No guard. Just truth.

Agatha hesitated.
Then nodded.
Once.
Shaky. Small. Real.

Rio exhaled like it was the first breath she hadn’t had to fight for.

She eased them both down into the bed, slow and careful, like she didn’t want to jostle the fragile peace between them. Her arms came around Agatha again, sure and steady. And Agatha let herself fall into them.

Not a kiss.
Not sex.
Just warmth. Skin. Breath. A closeness that felt almost unbearable in how much it asked for.

Agatha tucked her face in against Rio’s neck.

She stared at the place where Rio’s pulse beat steady beneath her skin.

She felt a kiss pressed to the top of her head.
Felt Rio’s arms tighten just slightly.

And in that quiet, Agatha breathed. Felt her body finally relax.

She was still scared.
Still unsure.

But she no longer felt alone.

Chapter Fifteen

Agatha blinked awake.

The room was dark—soft blue shadows pooling in the corners, a faint gold glow bleeding under the door from the hallway. Her limbs felt heavy. Her eyes gritty. Her body sore in a way that wasn’t exactly painful but still made her shift under the covers like she’d been wrung out and left to dry.

She didn’t know what time it was. Her phone was somewhere. Probably dead. Everything was quiet.

Too quiet.

And she was still naked. Still in her bed. But tucked in.

A sharp pulse of confusion went through her, quick and tight.

She didn’t remember falling asleep.

The last thing she remembered was—

Rio. Her hands. Her arms. Her voice, soft and close. I’m not going anywhere.

Agatha sat up slowly, blanket slipping off her shoulder. Her skin was cool. Exposed. She pulled the sheet tighter around her chest and scanned the room.

Empty.

Her stomach dropped.

It wasn’t rational—she knew that—but the ache hit hard and fast anyway.

Rio was gone?

Of course she left. Of course. You fell asleep like a fucking idiot after sobbing all over her and now she’s done. She’s done. You pushed her too far. You always—

A crash broke the silence.

Metal on tile. A muffled curse.

Agatha startled so hard she nearly toppled off the bed. Then froze.

Because it was coming from the kitchen.

She held her breath.

Another sound—softer this time. A clink of something ceramic. A quiet hum. That voice.

Rio.

Her heart squeezed so hard it felt like something inside her cracked.

She let out a breath. Pressed a hand to her chest.

Still here.

Still here.

And the fear didn't go completely away—not really—but it changed shape. Melted into something smaller. Something that made her eyes sting and her ribs expand, and the thought thank god rattle loose in her head like a prayer she’d never admit to saying.

She gathered the blanket tighter around herself and swung her legs over the edge of the bed. Her knees cracked. Her body ached. Her hair was a crime.

But she stood.

Agatha paused at the doorway, glancing toward her dresser. A beat. Then another. Her eyes found the oversized shirt draped across the back of a chair in the corner—one of Rio’s, probably. Or maybe it was hers. Hard to tell anymore. It smelled like laundry detergent and something softer beneath it. Something lived-in. Like Rio.

She shrugged it on without thinking.

It hung off one shoulder, too big in the sleeves, loose around the waist. It didn’t quite cover everything, but it was enough to keep her from feeling completely bare. Her body still felt wrung out, like a wire that had finally gone slack, and part of her wanted to crawl back under the sheets and pretend she hadn’t panicked just now. But her feet were already moving.

The hallway was dim, but the kitchen glowed faintly ahead—soft, golden, like something out of a painting. She heard it again: the low hum of Rio’s voice. Not singing, exactly. More like murmuring to herself. And the clink of something being set down gently.

Agatha rounded the corner.

Silent as a ghost.

And Rio—barefoot bu the fridge, hoodie swallowing her frame, boxers slung low on her hips, face lit up like a painting in the fridge light—nearly jumped out of her skin when Agatha said, deadpan:

"This your version of a wake-up call?"

Rio yelped.

Actually yelped.

Then spun, hand to her chest like she’d just seen the devil. "Jesus Christ, Aggie!"

Agatha smirked, leaning against the doorframe. "Good morning to you too."

Rio recovered quickly, trying to cover the flinch with a scowl. "I was making you tea. And toast."

Agatha arched an eyebrow. "You mean you were making noise and burning bread."

Rio gestured to the toaster. "I’ll have you know that my toast is perfectly edible. Probably."

A pause. Not awkward, just... full. Quiet buzz between them.

Agatha crossed the kitchen slowly, bare feet soft against the tile. She stopped beside the counter, glancing down at the mug Rio had abandoned.

Her fingers brushed the handle.

 

“Chamomile?” she asked, voice lower now.

Rio nodded. “Didn’t know what else to do. Thought you might want something warm.”

Agatha looked at her. Really looked. And for once, didn’t try to look away.

“Why’d you stay?” she asked.

Rio leaned back against the counter. Shrugged one shoulder. “You were hurting. I didn’t want to leave you like that.”

Agatha swallowed. “You didn’t have to stay.”

“I wanted to,” Rio said simply. “Even if you’d kicked me out. I would've still made tea first.”

A beat.

“I keep fucking it up,” Agatha admitted.

Rio’s expression didn’t change. Just softened. “So do I.”

Agatha looked up. Surprised. “You?”

“I let you push me away too easily,” Rio said. “I pretended it didn’t hurt when it did. I pushed you too hard. I made rules so you wouldn’t run, but maybe I should’ve just... said how I felt. From the start.”

She paused.

“I should’ve told you I was falling.”

The words knocked the air out of Agatha’s lungs.

She blinked. “You were?”

Rio gave her a look. “Aggie. I am.”

Silence again. This one different. Stunned.

“I thought I was protecting myself,” Agatha whispered. “By staying in control. By keeping it simple. But I wasn’t.”

Rio stepped closer. “What were you doing?”

Agatha’s throat bobbed. “I was building a wall. And then wondering why it felt lonely inside it.”

Rio’s hand twitched, like she wanted to reach out but didn’t want to push.

Agatha saw it. Closed the gap herself, her hand wrapping around hers.

“I want to try,” she said. Voice trembling. “I don’t know what this is or where it could go. But I want to try.”

Rio’s eyes went soft, shiny at the edges. “Me too.”

They stood there for a breathless moment, nothing between them but air and everything they hadn’t said.

Then Rio tugged Agatha gently by the hand, pulling her in closer until their faces were only a breath away. Agatha’s breath caught, her eyes flicking down to Rio’s mouth before she closed the distance.

It was the softest kiss they’d ever shared. No smirk. No games. No pressure.
Just lips. Just warmth. Just breath.

And it didn’t feel like breaking a rule.
It felt like finally telling the truth.

Agatha’s hand found the front of Rio’s hoodie and curled into it without thinking. Not to pull her closer. Just to hold on. To anchor herself in the middle of the kitchen at what was probably 4AM, barefoot and bare-souled, wrapped in a shirt that wasn’t hers, kissing the girl who was.

Rio’s lips moved like she was memorising her. Careful. Slow. Like she was trying to carve this moment into her bones.

Agatha couldn’t help the smile that took over her face.
A real one. Small. Unsteady.

The kiss broke, soft and natural, like a tide receding.
And for a beat, their foreheads stayed pressed together.

Agatha’s breath caught—then slipped out again in a quiet, breathy chuckle. Not sharp. Not mocking. Just full of something tired and tender and almost disbelieving.

Rio’s mouth tilted, the hint of a grin tugging at the corner. Her eyes fluttered open.

They were both smiling.

It wasn’t perfect. Wasn’t some movie-ending, fireworks-behind-the-eyes kind of moment. It was quiet. Fragile. Like if either of them breathed too hard, it might dissolve.

But it held.

Agatha pulled back just enough to look at her properly. Her thumb brushed against the edge of Rio’s hoodie string, twisting it once. “You really made toast?”

Rio looked deeply offended. “You say that like it’s not a culinary achievement.”

Agatha glanced over her shoulder toward the toaster, where two very charred pieces of bread sat like tiny monuments to hubris. “You almost set off the smoke alarm again, didn’t you.”

Rio hesitated. “...I handled it.”

A soft snort escaped Agatha’s nose before she could stop it.

God. How long had it been since she’d felt like this?

Warm. Light. Like her chest wasn’t a war zone. Like she wasn’t two seconds away from bolting. Like maybe—maybe—this could be safe.

Rio scratched the back of her neck. “I panicked. You were sleeping. I didn’t want to leave, but I didn’t want to just sit there, and I thought maybe you’d want something when you woke up, and—yeah. Okay. I made the world’s worst breakfast.”

Agatha’s fingers drifted to the edge of the counter. “I like that you tried.”

Rio looked at her for a long second. Then reached out and gently linked their pinkies together. Not a full handhold. Just that. Light. Careful. Like she didn’t want to startle her.

“You don’t have to say everything at once,” Rio murmured. “I know it’s a lot. I just… I need to know we’re on the same page. That you’re not going to pretend this doesn’t matter tomorrow.”

Agatha nodded. Her voice was rough when it came. “It matters.”

“You matter,” Rio said, almost instantly. And then, quieter, like it slipped out: “You always did.”

Agatha blinked hard. Her throat felt thick again, but not from panic this time.

“I kept thinking,” she said, “that if I wanted this too much, it’d hurt more when it ended. So I tried to… ration it. Control it.”

Rio tilted her head. “How’s that working out for you?”

Agatha let out a soft, wry breath. “Terribly.”

A beat.

Then Rio stepped in closer. Their foreheads bumped lightly again.

“No more rules?” she asked.

“No more rules,” Agatha whispered.

Rio grinned, relieved. “Even the no-sleepover one?”

Agatha gave her a look. “Like we ever actually kept that one in the first place.”

Rio hummed. “True. I’ve basically lived here for a week. Should’ve started paying rent.”

“You contribute in your own way,” Agatha said, deadpan. “Mostly by taking up all the hot water and leaving your socks all over the apartment.”

Rio gasped, mock wounded. “Those socks are artistic statements. You’re just uncultured.”

Agatha leaned in, the edge of a smirk tugging at her lips. “If by ‘artistic’ you mean mildly damp and hidden between the cushions on my lounge—”

“That happened once.”

“Twice.”

“Okay, but in my defense,” Rio murmured, stepping even closer, “you make it very hard to focus on laundry when you walk around in nothing but one of my shirts.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “So it’s my fault you’re a mess?”

“Completely,” Rio said, like it was obvious.

Their noses brushed. Agatha’s breath hitched, but her eyes stayed soft.

Then Rio kissed her again.

Not shy this time. Not tentative.

Just a slow, warm drag of lips. Familiar and new at once.

Agatha leaned into it with a small sound, her arms sliding up and around Rio’s neck. Her fingers found their way into her hair, curling there—soft but sure.

The kiss deepened for a moment. Then broke. Then started again, like a shared joke they didn’t want to end.

Agatha pulled back just enough to whisper, “I can’t believe I almost ruined this.”

Rio shook her head gently. “You didn’t. You paused. We’re unpausing.”

Another kiss. Quick this time. A punctuation mark.

Agatha exhaled against her mouth. “God, you’re annoying.”

Rio grinned. “And yet. Still here.”

“You say that like it’s a flex.”

“It absolutely is.” She stole another kiss. “You’re not easy, Agatha.”

Agatha hummed. “And you’re not subtle.”

Rio’s lips brushed her cheek. Her jaw. “You love it.”

“Unfortunately,” Agatha muttered, tilting her head to allow it. “Yeah. I think I do.”

They kept kissing—gentle, idle, stupid with affection. No agenda. Just the quiet thrill of still here. Still yours.

Rio’s hand found Agatha’s waist under the hem of the shirt, fingers curling against bare skin.

Agatha didn’t flinch. Didn’t freeze.

She sighed. Relaxed into it. Smiled against Rio’s mouth.

And murmured, “You burn the toast again, I’m kicking you out.”

Rio laughed. “Fair.”

Then kissed her again—longer this time. Slower. Like she had nowhere else to be.

Agatha's hands stayed tangled in her hair, thumb brushing lightly at the nape of her neck. She didn’t want to let go. Didn’t plan to.

Outside, the sky was shifting—dark blue fading to lavender, then pink. A soft bleed of morning creeping through the windows, filling the kitchen with light.

They didn’t notice it at first.

But Agatha looked over Rio’s shoulder. Watched the edges of the world begin to glow.

The sun was coming up.
And for the first time in weeks, Agatha wasn’t afraid of the morning.

 

***

Boxes were everywhere. Half-labelled, half-open, and mostly filled with things Agatha had forgotten she even owned.

Somewhere in the chaos was a toaster she hadn’t used since 2019. In another: three different mugs that said World’s Best Boss, none of which she remembered buying. Her back ached. Her knees crackled every time she crouched. Her hair was up in a clip that was hanging on for dear life and losing.

And Rio was singing off-key in the living room.

They were doing it.
They were actually doing it.
Moving in.
Together.

Because what was the point of two rent payments when they were already inseparable? Agatha had spent the last four weeks waking up tangled in Rio’s sheets more often than her own. Her apartment had become a glorified laundry basket. Half her life had already migrated over—bras in the bathroom, snacks in the pantry, her favourite coffee mug showing up in Rio’s sink every morning like it had chosen a side.

It made sense.

What didn’t make sense was how they’d decided whose apartment to keep.

That had been a war.

Agatha had brought logic: more storage, better water pressure, glorious natural light.
Rio had brought… other tactics.
Tactics involving a “debate” that left Agatha flat on her back, gasping, thighs still trembling as Rio leaned over her and said smugly, “So. My place?”

Agatha had muttered, “This is emotional manipulation.”
Rio had kissed her shoulder and replied, “No, it’s just really good sex.”

Agatha had grumbled. But she’d agreed.

On one condition.

“As soon as we can,” she’d said the next morning, tugging Rio’s hoodie over her head, “we move out of this complex. I’m tired of the neighbours giving us the ‘we-heard-you-last-night’ face every time we walk past.”

Rio—holding two coffees and exactly zero shame—had just said, “To be fair, they did hear us last night. We were loud.”

You were loud, Agatha had corrected, snatching her mug.

Rio had winked. “You loved it.”

Agatha had not responded.

Now, a month later, their lives were spilling into the same drawers. One apartment. Two toothbrushes. Three kinds of oat milk because neither of them remembered which one they actually liked.

Agatha stood in the doorway, surrounded by the chaos of moving—boxes and stray socks and the unmistakable scent of takeout—and watched Rio crouch in front of a half-assembled bookshelf with the wrong screwdriver and an alarming amount of confidence.

It was meant to be a bookshelf.
So far, it looked like a modern art piece titled Lesbian Failure.

Agatha stepped over a box labelled winter stuff?—a lie; it contained one mitten and a tangled phone charger—and leaned against the doorframe, arms crossed.

“Wrong screwdriver,” she said, sipping lukewarm coffee from a chipped mug that neither of them could claim ownership of.

Rio didn’t look up. “No, it’s not.”

“It absolutely is.”

“I know what I’m doing.”

“You really don’t.”

“I’m building us a future,” Rio muttered.

Agatha blinked. “Out of pine composite and blind optimism?”

“IKEA is a metaphor, Aggie. Let me work.”

Her lips twitched, but she didn’t quite smile. Not fully. Not yet. It still felt too new. Too fragile. This whole thing—boxes and keys and toothbrush holders. There was a shelf in the bathroom now with both their skincare. Side by side. Like it had always been that way.

Like this wasn’t something that could still shatter.

She swallowed.

It was too quiet again, save for the occasional clink of tools and Rio’s soft curses. The apartment smelled like cardboard, clean sweat, and the vaguely citrusy detergent Rio used on her hoodies. Agatha had thrown one on this morning without thinking. The sleeves hung over her fingers, ridiculous and soft, and somehow that made her feel more exposed than being naked.

She cleared her throat. “If this shelf collapses and crushes your foot, I’m not taking you to the hospital.”

“Rude.”

“I’ll call you an Uber. That’s love.”

She froze.

Love.

The word snapped like a rubber band in the air between them. Too casual. Too dangerous. Too close to something she hadn’t dared name.

She felt it the second it left her mouth. The atmosphere shifted. Subtle. Sharp. Like a dropped plate that hadn’t shattered—yet.

Rio looked up.

Not startled. Not smug. Just… still.

Agatha didn’t dare meet her eyes.

Fuck. Fuck.

It didn’t count. It was a joke. A throwaway. People said that’s love all the time. It didn’t mean—

“Agatha,” Rio said. Soft. No heat. Just her name, like it meant something.

Agatha cleared her throat again, louder. “Don’t read into it.”

“I didn’t say anything.”

“You’re doing the face.”

“What face?”

“The one that means you’re thinking.”

“I’m always thinking.”

“Exactly. Stop.”

Rio leaned back on her heels. Her hoodie had a smear of something—grease? chocolate? glue?—and she looked like she hadn’t slept in two days.

She looked like home.

Agatha hated how badly she wanted to say it again.

Instead, she shrugged. “Shelf’s still broken.”

Rio didn’t blink. “You meant it, didn’t you?”

Silence settled in the spaces between boxes and tangled extension cords.

Agatha hesitated. Her skin prickled. She wished Rio would go back to fumbling screws or talking nonsense about symbolism. Anything but this.

She swallowed. “What if I did?”

It cracked something open. Quiet, trembling, real.

Rio didn’t smirk. Didn’t deflect.

Then, softly: “Then I guess you’re not the only one.”

Agatha finally looked at her.

And Rio was still there.

Kneeling in cardboard, surrounded by mess, ridiculous in every possible way—and still here.

The breath left Agatha’s lungs in a stuttering exhale.

Then she dropped to her knees beside her.

Not graceful. Her knee cracked loudly. A corner of a box stabbed her in the calf. She didn’t care.

She reached out and plucked the screwdriver from Rio’s hand.

“I’ve got it,” she said, voice low but steady. “Before you finish whatever crime against geometry you’ve started.”

Rio blinked. “I loosened one screw.”

“And tilted the entire shelf like it’s auditioning to be the Leaning Tower of Pisa.” Agatha squinted at the lopsided mess. “Honestly, I don’t even know how you managed to get that mirror on the wall across from the bed with this level of skill.”

Rio choked. “It’s secure!”

“It’s diagonal.”

“It’s artful!”

“It’s horny.”

Rio grinned. “Well, yeah.”

Agatha shook her head, inspecting the mess in front of them. She lined up the screwdriver—too short, the wrong shape entirely—and sighed. “Unreal. I fall in love with a woman who strategically mounts sex mirrors like a pervert.”

Rio’s breath hitched.

Agatha noticed.
Of course she noticed.

She didn’t look up. Just adjusted her grip and jammed the too-small screwdriver into the misaligned screw with the grim determination of someone who’d decided love meant improvising.

It groaned in protest. So did her wrist.

But the screw turned.

Agatha smirked, faint and fond. “This is the wrong tool, you know.”

Rio blinked. “It’s the only one we have.”

“Exactly,” Agatha murmured, twisting it tighter. “So I’m making it work.”

She felt Rio still holding her breath beside her.

Then: “You said it again,” Rio said, voice quiet. Not teasing. Just... soft.

“Did I?”

“Yeah.”

Agatha twisted one more screw into place, steady now, even as her pulse picked up. She didn’t look away from the shelf. But her voice was gentler than it had been in days. “Well,” she muttered. “I do.”
Then she looked at her. Met her eyes, fully and completely.
“I love you.”

Rio didn’t move. Then she scooched forward, cardboard creaking beneath her knees, until she was right there beside her—elbow to elbow. Shoulder to shoulder.

“You mean that?” she asked—not doubting, just confirming. Needing to hear it one more time.

Agatha nodded. “Yeah. I mean it.”

Her voice didn’t shake.

Her hands did.

Rio leaned in and kissed her.

No bells. No crescendo.

Just warm lips and the scent of home. The heat of skin and familiarity and the quiet knowledge that sometimes, after everything, you still get to choose someone.

Agatha sighed into it. Her fingers curled in the front of Rio’s hoodie like they were built to fit there.

When they pulled apart, foreheads rested together. Still close. Still breathing the same breath.

Rio’s voice was quiet. “I love you too, you know.”

Agatha closed her eyes.
Let the words settle into her bones. Let herself believe them.

She smiled—slow, unsteady. Like it snuck up on her.

Because this girl—this ridiculous, chaotic, barefoot girl in a hoodie and grease-stained boxers, surrounded by cardboard and half-built furniture—had wormed her way into Agatha’s life with bad jokes and stubborn warmth and a mouth that never knew when to quit.

And God help her.
She was everything Agatha had said she didn’t want.
Too young. Too loud. Too much.

And somehow…
She was everything Agatha needed.

Her thumb brushed the edge of Rio’s jaw. Light. Thoughtless.

“Turns out,” she whispered, “you’re exactly my type.”

Rio’s mouth curled into a grin. “Knew it.”

Agatha groaned, smiling anyway. “God, you’re annoying.”

Rio kissed her again—quick, smug, unbearable.

“And yet,” she murmured against her mouth, “you’re tragically in love with me.”

Agatha didn’t argue.
Didn’t pull away.

She just let herself stay.

Because somehow in the middle of cardboard chaos and a bookshelf that still leaned a little too far left, this wasn’t a disaster waiting to happen.

This was home.
